201504	8	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	I think all of you know that Brian served as director of the division and as FOMC secretary from 2007 to 2010.	5	5
201504	9	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Since he retired from the Board, Brian has been a visiting professor in the Department of Economics at Georgetown University.	5	5
201504	10	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Now, as I think many of you know, in recent years, the job of director of the Division of Monetary Affairs has become increasingly burdensome.	5	5
201504	11	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	It has entailed serving as the Committee’s chief monetary policy advisor, as secretary of the FOMC, and as leader of a large organization with critical responsibilities.	5	5
201504	12	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	As part of a strategy to create a more sustainable situation, Brian will have oversight responsibility for the FOMC Secretariat and will play a key role in the production of the minutes and transcripts of FOMC meetings.	5	5
201504	13	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Obviously, these are things he has done superbly well in the past and for which he is eminently well qualified.	5	5
201504	14	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Accordingly, I intend to propose that Brian be appointed by the FOMC as its secretary.	5	5

201504	16	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Under this arrangement, Thomas will continue to serve as the Committee’s primary advisor on monetary policy and will also be able to dedicate more of his energy to ensuring that the Division of Monetary Affairs fulfills its critical role in supporting our monetary policy and other responsibilities.	5	5

201504	22	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Our first item is financial developments and open market operations, and let me call on Simon to deliver the Desk report.	61	6
201504	23	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201504	24	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Lorie and I will split the briefing into three parts.	61	6
201504	25	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	First, I will review financial market developments.	61	6
201504	26	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Next, Lorie will review Desk operations.	61	6
201504	27	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Finally, I will discuss staff work on enhancing the calculation methodology for the federal funds effective rate.	61	6
201504	28	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, domestic financial conditions eased following more-accommodative-than-expected US monetary policy communications and weaker-than-expected economic data, including the March employment report.	61	6
201504	29	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	On net, nominal Treasury rates declined by as many as 25 basis points, the S&P 500 index gained 2 percent, and the DXY dollar index decreased nearly 3 percent.	61	6
201504	30	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	A substantial portion of these changes came around the time of the March FOMC events, which were characterized as being more accommodative than expected despite the removal of “patient” language from the statement.	61	6
201504	31	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Investors pointed, in particular, to the large downward shift in the target federal funds rate projections in the SEP and, to a lesser extent, the downward revisions to Committee participants’ projections of inflation, GDP growth, and the longer-run unemployment rate.	61	6
201504	32	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The left column of your top-left panel shows that nominal and real interest rates declined in the one-hour window around the statement and SEP releases, while measures of inflation compensation rose, equity prices increased, and the dollar weakened.	61	6
201504	33	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the right column of the table, the absolute magnitudes of these moves were very large relative to changes in one-hour windows around FOMC statement releases over the past decade.	61	6
201504	34	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	One hypothesis for seeing moves of this magnitude could be decreased market liquidity.	61	6
201504	35	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Indeed, late in the trading session outside the window used to measure these FOMC announcement effects, there was a very large move in the euro‒dollar currency pair.	61	6
201504	36	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The move pushed the intraday trading range for the currency pair to over 4 percent, a 5 standard deviation move over the period since 2004, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201504	37	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The size of the move is comparable to the 6 standard deviation range in the 10-year Treasury yield on October 15, both of which took place amid very high volumes.	61	6
201504	38	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The March FOMC events shifted out expectations for the timing of liftoff according to the Desk surveys, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201504	39	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The “flash” survey, taken three business days after the March FOMC meeting, suggests that most of the shift occurred in response to the meeting and the large price moves in the hour following the March FOMC statement release, therefore likely reflecting shifting policy expectations as opposed to outsized liquidity effects.	61	6
201504	40	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Since the flash survey, soft domestic economic data and speeches from Federal Reserve officials appear to have further solidified this shift in policy expectations.	61	6
201504	41	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The April surveys also showed a notably slower expected pace of policy normalization after liftoff.	61	6
201504	42	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The middle-right panel shows that the probability distribution for the pace of tightening in the first year after liftoff, assuming no return to the zero bound, shifted toward a slower pace over the period, the first notable shift in these views since the question was originally asked last September.	61	6
201504	43	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	A similar shift occurred in the distribution of the expected pace of tightening in the second year after liftoff.	61	6
201504	44	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	In considering when the Federal Reserve will begin to normalize monetary policy, market participants are particularly focused on the outlook for inflation and the Committee’s reasonable confidence that inflation will move back to its 2 percent objective.	61	6
201504	45	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	We asked survey respondents to score the importance of various factors they believe the Committee will use in assessing whether reasonable confidence in the inflation outlook has been achieved.	61	6
201504	46	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-left panel, respondents assigned the most importance to a further improvement in the labor market and the absence of weakening in realized core inflation.	61	6
201504	47	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, market-based measures of inflation compensation increased alongside higher energy prices and a weaker US dollar, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201504	48	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Forward measures of inflation compensation increased at both shorter- and longer-dated horizons but remain below levels at the end of 2013.	61	6
201504	49	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The increases over the period were attributed to the March FOMC communications, somewhat higher-than-expected realized inflation, the increase in oil prices, and positioning dynamics in the TIPS market.	61	6
201504	50	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Longer-term inflation expectations from Desk surveys were little changed over the period.	61	6
201504	51	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Meanwhile, front-month Brent crude increased nearly 22 percent but remains more than 40 percent lower since the end of 2013.	61	6
201504	52	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As I noted, the DXY dollar index declined nearly 3 percent over the intermeeting period but is over 20 percent higher since the end of 2013.	61	6
201504	53	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Despite the depreciation over the period, market participants expect the exchange value of the US dollar to continue its broad appreciation amid ongoing monetary policy divergence across major economies.	61	6
201504	54	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Desk dealer survey respondents reported that dollar appreciation seen since last summer has prompted them to revise lower their forecasts for 2015 growth and inflation, with the median markdowns to 2015 GDP growth and core PCE inflation of roughly 40 basis points and 20 basis points, respectively.	61	6
201504	55	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	A key factor contributing to broad dollar strength has been widening global interest rate differentials, especially between the United States and the euro area.	61	6
201504	56	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	These interest rate differentials became more pronounced as euro-area sovereign rates have traded increasingly negative and yield curves have flattened substantially.	61	6
201504	57	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The top-left panel of your next exhibit shows the extent of negative rate trading by country and maturity.	61	6
201504	58	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Red indicates that 100 percent of the bonds in that category trade at a negative yield, while green indicates that none trade negative.	61	6
201504	59	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Despite the continued decline in euro-area rates and the increasing universe of securities trading at negative yields, there have been few market-functioning issues, and the ECB has stated that it has had little trouble achieving its purchase targets thus far.	61	6
201504	60	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Even so, it is possible that market functioning strains will emerge over time, and to help address such strains, the ECB unveiled details of an augmented securities- lending program aimed at supporting bond and repo market liquidity.	61	6
201504	61	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The declines in euro-area rates, coupled with the very large currency depreciation and increase in equities, have substantially eased European financial conditions since President Draghi’s remarks at the Jackson Hole symposium last August.	61	6
201504	62	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	It is interesting to compare the asset price reaction with recent LSAP programs.	61	6
201504	63	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Using the price changes from when asset purchase expectations began to form until three months after the purchase programs were announced, the ECB’s PSPP and BOJ’s QQE, shown in the left and middle columns of the top-right panel, respectively, contributed to significant currency depreciation and meaningful equity price increases.	61	6
201504	64	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The ECB’s program resulted in large declines in German nominal forward rates, but it has not been accompanied by an increase in longer-dated forward inflation measures.	61	6
201504	65	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	In comparison, Japanese policies supported a large rise in forward inflation compensation and a pronounced increase in equities, perhaps stemming from the focus on reaching the new higher inflation target.	61	6
201504	66	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	By contrast, US asset price reactions to LSAP3 were more limited, as the right column shows— though it did have a large effect in the mortgage markets, which is not included in the panel.	61	6
201504	67	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	One potential flashpoint for financial markets is the highly fluid situation in Greece.	61	6
201504	68	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	While Greek asset prices have responded sharply to recent developments, the broader market reaction to perceived downside risks in Greece has been relatively muted and perhaps a bit complacent.	61	6
201504	69	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Market participants attribute the lack of spillovers to institutional improvements in the euro area, reduced private-sector exposure to Greece, and the effects of ECB asset purchases.	61	6
201504	70	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Reflecting the mounting liquidity pressure from deposit flight and bank funding strains, Greek banks have also increased their borrowing via the emergency liquidity assistance program to €76 billion in April from €69 billion in March.	61	6
201504	71	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As would be expected, Greece’s Target2 liability, which represents balances owed to others in the Eurosystem, rose in March, shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201504	72	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	This level is near Greece’s prior peak Target2 liability in June 2012.	61	6
201504	73	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	It is uncertain how long the Greek government will be able to meet its debt obligations.	61	6
201504	74	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants still expect an agreement between Greece and its creditors to be reached but only after a high-stakes game of brinkmanship.	61	6
201504	75	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Steve will further discuss Greece in his briefing.	61	6
201504	76	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Shifting to emerging markets, there has been a very sharp increase in Chinese equities over recent months, shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201504	77	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, mainland Chinese and Hong Kong equities rose by 23 percent and 16 percent, respectively, and, over the past year, the Shanghai Composite has more than doubled.	61	6
201504	78	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Mainland equity outperformance came despite a worsening domestic economic outlook and probably involved some speculative dynamics, though it was supported by expected and actual monetary policy easing.	61	6
201504	79	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	During the intermeeting period, the People’s Bank of China cut their reserve requirement ratio by a larger-than-expected 100 basis points; most contacts expect additional cuts to reserve requirements or decreases in lending and deposit rates in the near term.	61	6
201504	80	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Equity prices in other emerging markets also increased, and, as shown in the bottom-left panel, broader EM asset prices rose, partially retracing prior period declines.	61	6
201504	81	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The moves were supported by the accommodative March FOMC communication as well as a moderate abatement of risks in a number of countries, including Brazil and Russia.	61	6
201504	82	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	This partial retracement of emerging market asset prices came despite continued markdowns of expected growth in several countries.	61	6
201504	83	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	These markdowns and recent US dollar strength have contributed to a broader trend of emerging market currency depreciation since the May 2013 JEC testimony or so- called taper tantrum.	61	6
201504	84	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants are concerned that taper tantrum–like volatility in emerging markets could materialize as the Federal Reserve approaches normalization.	61	6
201504	85	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Recall that implied volatility in emerging market currencies rose sharply with US interest rate implied volatility in spring 2013, shown in the bottom-right panel, and has recently moved back to similar levels.	61	6
201504	86	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Decelerating emerging market growth and rising corporate leverage, as well as volatility in commodity prices may make emerging markets vulnerable as normalization nears.	61	6
201504	87	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	However, these risks are somewhat offset by lower emerging market asset valuations and reportedly more cautious positioning from emerging market investors, as discussed in the special QS memo.	61	6
201504	88	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Volatility in emerging markets is only one part of broader financial market volatility that some worry could ensue from expected Federal Reserve normalization.	61	6
201504	89	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Indeed, a senior IMF official recently warned of a “super taper tantrum,” in which negative term premiums would be rapidly decompressed as domestic policy rates are increased; Thomas will comment more on this risk in his briefing.	61	6
201504	90	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Given the punctuated bouts of recent realized volatility in the very deep and liquid markets I discussed earlier, financial market volatility during normalization could be even more challenging for relatively illiquid markets.	61	6
201504	91	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	I will now take questions before turning to Lorie.	61	6

201504	94	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201504	95	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	I’ll start with exhibit 3 and provide an update on MBS reinvestments, discuss testing of normalization tools, and conclude with the staff recommendation to extend the existing central bank liquidity and swap arrangements.	61	6
201504	96	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk’s MBS reinvestment operations continue to go smoothly, and MBS market liquidity remains stable.	61	6
201504	97	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The continued trend toward higher prepayment speeds in March was largely an ongoing result of the low mortgage rates witnessed earlier in the year and has pushed the current monthly reinvestment amount up to approximately $40 billion, as shown in the top-left panel of your third exhibit.	61	6
201504	98	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Despite the increased size of reinvestments, we do not anticipate having any issues with the execution of MBS operations, but we have increased the frequency of our operations to accommodate their larger size.	61	6
201504	99	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Testing of the Federal Reserve’s overnight and term RRP operations continued over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201504	100	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Patterns of total RRP demand remained broadly consistent with recent experience, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201504	101	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The additional 25 counterparties that began participating in operations on March 16 have only modestly affected overall RRP usage.	61	6
201504	102	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	For broader perspective on the Federal Reserve’s involvement in reverse repo activity, this panel also includes reverse repos conducted with foreign official institutions, known as the “foreign RP pool,” shown in gray.	61	6
201504	103	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The size of the foreign RP pool is notably above its pre-crisis levels, largely a reflection of central banks’ desire to hold greater dollar liquidity buffers, while at the same time they are tightening their counterparty risk-management frameworks.	61	6
201504	104	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Increases in the foreign RP pool this period, and since the beginning of the year, have been primarily driven by a single customer who has sought to increase the liquidity profile of its FX reserves due to precautionary financial-stability motivations, in part by raising its cash balance held at the Federal Reserve.	61	6
201504	105	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk conducted two term operations over March quarter-end, the first a $75 billion, 14-day operation and the second a $125 billion, 7-day operation, summarized in your middle-left panel.	61	6
201504	106	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	This $200 billion offering in term RRPs reduced the Federal Reserve’s overall RRP offered amount spanning quarter-end to $500 billion, down from the $600 billion offered at year-end.	61	6
201504	107	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, the reduction did not appear to have an adverse effect on markets or meaningfully change participation, likely because the amount offered was perceived to still provide ample headroom above expected demand.	61	6
201504	108	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The 14-day operation was modestly oversubscribed, with $81 billion in propositions and a stop-out rate of 9 basis points, a slightly higher rate than was expected.	61	6
201504	109	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The 7-day operation conducted on March 30 was undersubscribed, with $101 billion in propositions submitted and a stop-out rate at the max offering rate of 10 basis points, similar to the rates on the undersubscribed operations held closer to year-end.	61	6
201504	110	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Substitution between overnight and term RRPs and the breakdown of counterparty demand at the March term operations were broadly similar to behavior observed in December.	61	6
201504	111	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in your middle-right panel, the Desk’s RRP operations continued to provide a soft floor under short-term interest rates, even around quarter-end.	61	6
201504	112	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The federal funds effective rate averaged 12 basis points over the period and printed at 6 basis points on quarter-end.	61	6
201504	113	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	While rates and volumes in unsecured markets over quarter-end were broadly in line with expectations, temporary funding pressures in secured markets were much larger than expected, with the overnight GCF repo index for Treasury collateral, shown in the dark blue line, printing at 45 basis points.	61	6
201504	114	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Further, the dispersion in repo rates increased notably.	61	6
201504	115	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	For example, the spread between rates on overnight Treasury GCF repo and triparty repo widened considerably on quarter-end.	61	6
201504	116	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	This spread, shown in your bottom-left panel, reached 30 basis points on quarter-end.	61	6
201504	117	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	While all the factors that drove the larger-than- expected widening between repo rates are not fully understood, institutions with stable access to triparty repo funding appeared to demand increased compensation to intermediate between triparty cash lenders, like money funds, and GCF borrowers, such as smaller or less creditworthy dealers.	61	6
201504	118	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	It should also be noted that the spread between GCF and triparty repo rates has been gradually widening over the past several months even outside quarter-end.	61	6
201504	119	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	This trend is likely partially driven by financial institutions modifying behavior in response to regulatory changes and associated higher costs to intermediate between triparty and GCF repo markets.	61	6
201504	120	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Looking forward, pursuant to the resolution adopted at the March FOMC meeting, the staff proposes conducting term RRP tests over June quarter-end.	61	6
201504	121	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	For the June quarter-end, we suggest a slightly different approach to the public communication about the term RRPs than was used in December and March.	61	6
201504	122	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	As outlined in your bottom-right panel, the Desk proposes to release a statement shortly after the April FOMC meeting minutes on May 20 that would note the tentative intention to offer at least $200 billion of term RRPs in addition to capacity of overnight RRPs for the June quarter-end.	61	6
201504	123	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Based on our experience with the March term operations, we believe that $200 billion in term RRP capacity over June quarter- end, in combination with at least $300 billion capacity in overnight RRP, should provide sufficient headroom on total RRP availability, assuming no change in the target range.	61	6
201504	124	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Further, we would propose noting in the statement that the Desk would release the remaining details on Monday, June 22—that is, after the June FOMC meeting.	61	6
201504	125	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	We would thus come back to the Committee with a recommendation of the exact size and maximum offering rate for each operation at or shortly after the June meeting.	61	6
201504	126	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	This communication approach could be replicated in future quarter-ends and should provide the market with confidence in available supply around quarter- ends, but, importantly, retain some flexibility to adjust the specific parameters of the operations should the Committee decide to lift off.	61	6
201504	127	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	In order to maintain operational readiness with the TDF—both within the Federal Reserve and among banks—the staff is developing plans to resume a routine, every- other-month testing schedule that would be similar to that employed prior to the series of special larger test operations conducted over the past year.	61	6
201504	128	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Offering rates, counterparty limits, and other terms of these operations would be set so that the scale of such testing operations would be modest.	61	6
201504	129	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The tentative plan is to announce and resume the routine periodic testing beginning next month.	61	6
201504	130	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Additionally, the work on implementing changes to the methodology for calculating interest payments is proceeding according to schedule.	61	6
201504	131	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Comments on the Federal Register notice are due by the middle of May.	61	6
201504	132	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	If there are no major issues raised by those comments, the staff should be in a position to implement the new methodology before the June FOMC meeting as planned.	61	6
201504	133	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Your fourth exhibit begins with the focus of some market participants over the intermeeting period on the discussion of normalization tools that appeared in the March FOMC minutes.	61	6
201504	134	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Contacts specifically highlighted the discussion concerning temporarily elevated capacity for the ON RRP facility.	61	6
201504	135	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	In the Desk’s April surveys, respondents were asked to provide their expectations for both the level of the daily aggregate cap and level of ON RRP demand around the time of liftoff.	61	6
201504	136	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, 10 respondents expected there to be no cap on the ON RRP facility immediately following liftoff.	61	6
201504	137	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Among those respondents expecting a cap at liftoff, the median expectation was a cap of $500 billion, and all anticipated that ON RRP demand would be at or below the cap.	61	6
201504	138	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Across all respondents, regardless of whether they expected a cap, the median expected level of ON RRP demand immediately after liftoff was $300 billion, unchanged from the March survey.	61	6
201504	139	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, many respondents did update their expectations for ON RRP demand from the previous survey—both immediately after liftoff and one- and three-years ahead.	61	6
201504	140	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Expectations shifted in both directions, with a number of participants moving their expectations by several hundred billion dollars, perhaps pointing to significant uncertainly about the likely level of take-up.	61	6
201504	141	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Respondents were also asked about their expectations for the variation in ON RRP demand over various time horizons.	61	6
201504	142	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	They expected the variability of the ON RRP demand around the time of liftoff to be more elevated than recent experience, largely due to uncertainties over the mix of overnight and term RRPs as well as how regulatory reforms might affect money markets when rates rise from the zero lower bound.	61	6
201504	143	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	In terms of the expected levels of money market rates at liftoff, the median estimate across respondents for the level of the federal funds effective rate was 35 basis points—very close to the center of the expected target range.	61	6
201504	144	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The April surveys also asked respondents for the probability they attach to the level of the effective rate averaging within certain ranges during the month following liftoff.	61	6
201504	145	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, respondents assigned very high probabilities to the effective rate being within the target range and only a negligible probability to the effective rate being outside the range.	61	6
201504	146	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, as discussed in the memo sent to the Committee on April 15, we would like to ask the Committee to vote on the authorization to renew for another year the standing liquidity swap arrangements with foreign central banks and NAFA swap arrangements.	61	6
201504	147	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	While the liquidity arrangements were authorized for an indefinite period in October 2013, the FOMC has the ability to unilaterally terminate its participation with six months’ notice.	61	6
201504	148	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	This is similar to the NAFA swap arrangements with Mexico and Canada, which are renewable annually on or before December 15 of each year and require six months’ notice to terminate.	61	6
201504	149	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	The use of liquidity swap lines recently has been sparse, as shown in the middle- left panel, with demand limited to regularly scheduled seven-day dollar auctions held by the Bank of Japan over year-end and March quarter-end.	61	6
201504	150	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	While this is consistent with relatively calm conditions in dollar funding markets, we believe the swap lines are an important liquidity backstop, helping to maintain stability and confidence in global funding markets.	61	6
201504	151	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Additionally, liquidity swap and NAFA swap arrangements are tangible and constructive signals of cooperation among central banks, and their attendant costs are minimal.	61	6
201504	152	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Liquidity swap arrangements also support the approach that the Federal Reserve along with other major central banks have endorsed that there are “no technical obstacles” to central banks’ capabilities to provide liquidity quickly to a systemically important financial market utility.	61	6
201504	153	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	Therefore, the staff recommends that the Committee vote to renew the liquidity swap lines and NAFA arrangements.	61	6
201504	154	2015-04-29	meeting	LOGAN	I will now turn back to Simon to discuss the calculation methodology for the effective funds rate.	61	6
201504	155	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Thanks, Lorie.	61	6
201504	156	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As detailed in a memo circulated in advance of the meeting, the staff has assessed that there might be some merit in changing the calculation methodology underlying the federal funds effective rate concurrent with the change in data source to the FR 2420.	61	6
201504	157	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	We are interested in the Committee’s initial feedback on this assessment.	61	6
201504	158	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As you are aware, the federal funds effective rate is currently calculated as a volume-weighted mean.	61	6
201504	159	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	That is, each observed transaction rate is weighted by the share of total volume transacted at this rate, and the effective rate is the sum of these weighted rates.	61	6
201504	160	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The distribution of volume by rates for a particular day from the FR 2420 data is shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201504	161	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The staff’s assessment is that it may be more appropriate to calculate the effective rate as the median (that is, the 50th percentile) of the distribution rather than its mean.	61	6
201504	162	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-left panel, the volume-weighted median generates a statistic that is the same as, or very close to, the mean at most times except for the crisis period.	61	6
201504	163	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	However, on those occasions when the mean and median do differ significantly, the staff’s preliminary analysis shows that the median is typically a better measure of broad money market conditions across a wide range of situations.	61	6
201504	164	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Moreover, the median is much more robust to invalid data.	61	6
201504	165	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	In general, for an invalid transaction to affect the median, it must have a large volume attached to it, while the mean can be moved by an invalid transaction that has a more typical volume and rate.	61	6
201504	166	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The staff believes this characteristic of the median would enhance both the integrity of the effective federal funds rate as a reference rate as well its credibility as a monetary policy instrument.	61	6
201504	167	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	We look forward to your views on this subject, and, based on your feedback, the staff may present a plan to move forward at the June meeting.	61	6
201504	168	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201504	169	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	That concludes our remarks.	61	6
201504	170	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	61	6
201504	171	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Are there questions or comments, particularly in response to Simon’s request for comments on the federal funds rate?	62	6
201504	172	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	62	6
201504	173	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	62	6
201504	174	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I found that the staff memo and also the memo to Reserve Bank research directors made a pretty good case, to my mind, for using the volume-weighted median.	62	6
201504	175	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	It’s a better measure of financial conditions for all the reasons that you went through, Simon.	62	6
201504	176	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	In addition, it’s more difficult to manipulate.	62	6
201504	177	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	What I mean is, in theory, any trade moves a mean, whereas to move the median, it either needs to be further away or bigger.	62	6
201504	178	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	Anyway, I think it is a good case, and I guess I have two questions relating to when we do “socialize” this to the public, which we may not have the answers to today.	62	6
201504	179	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	One is, will a median versus a mean have a differential effect on existing contracts, of which there are many trillions?	62	6
201504	180	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	Two is, I’d be interested to hear how market participants react to this mean–median thing.	62	6
201504	181	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I think that the potential cost that’s laid out in the memo is that of successfully communicating it to the public.	62	6
201504	182	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I don’t really see that as an insurmountable concern.	62	6
201504	183	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I mean, very few people even know what the effective federal funds rate is in the first place, and the kind of people who know that are probably able to tell the difference between a volume-weighted mean and a median if they want to and need to.	62	6
201504	184	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I don’t see that as a big thing, but I would certainly be sensitive to the views of market participants on that.	62	6
201504	185	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	In terms of the contracts that are written on the effective federal funds rate, if we were to pursue this, there would be a long lead time during which the market participants would know that the change is coming.	62	6
201504	186	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	We would have to weigh the effect that that would have, and it would have some effect because the median is not always equal to the mean, but many of these contracts average over a long period of time.	62	6
201504	187	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	So occasions on particular days when we do see differences are probably not going to have a large effect on those contracts.	62	6
201504	188	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	What they will be perhaps more interested in is the level of rates that you’ll be setting in the future.	62	6
201504	189	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	If you think about a contract in 2016, that’s going to be very heavily influenced by where they think you’ll be setting the target rate.	62	6
201504	190	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The kinds of issues to do with the gap between the mean and the median are very second-order, compared with that.	62	6
201504	191	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	They also have to think of things like, “Where would the effective federal funds rate be trading in the range?,” and so on.	62	6
201504	192	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	I don’t believe this change is anything of first-order importance for a contract, and it’s pretty typical for the uncertainty that market participants face overall in terms of trading in the federal funds market, which we know some large participants have left and some other participants could leave in the future, affecting where the federal funds rate trades in the range.	62	6
201504	193	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	On the market participants’ knowledge of this, I agree that many people probably don’t know that much about the detailed calculation of the effective federal funds rate.	62	6
201504	194	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Those who do would find it pretty understandable, I believe, that we switch from a volume-weighted mean to a volume-weighted median, partly because one of the things that we do know is that the mean is quite heavily influenced by a small transaction at a rate that is far away from where most of the volume is.	62	6
201504	195	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	That’s helpful.	62	6
201504	196	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Any other comments?	62	6
201504	197	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	62	6
201504	198	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	62	6
201504	199	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	In the LIBOR case, the issue about really small changes in LIBOR from what was perceived to be a correct LIBOR pricing was considered a big issue.	62	6
201504	200	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Here you’ve got a picture of a 20 or 40 basis point difference.	62	6
201504	201	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	It gives me a little bit of pause that the people who are contracting on this might be upset by this change.	62	6
201504	202	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	In the crisis period, particularly as the balance sheet got larger, we didn’t have that much control over the federal funds rate, and that was an event that really was exogenous to the calculation method.	62	6
201504	203	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	Whichever calculation method we would have used, there would have been more variance at that time.	62	6
201504	204	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	If, arbitrarily, the Federal Reserve had turned up on one day and said, “We are going to change that calculation method,” without any kind of forewarning, that would make payments flow differentially to what people expected.	62	6
201504	205	2015-04-29	meeting	POTTER	The plan here is, if there is support for moving forward with this, it will be clearly communicated well in advance, and it will be the type of consideration that all market participants should have to take into account when pricing contracts.	62	6
201504	206	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you.	62	6
201504	207	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Any other comments?	62	6

201504	262	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Next, I think we’re going to move to our second topic, which is normalization procedures, and I’m going to call on Ellen Meade to provide a briefing.	96	9
201504	263	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	264	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	I will be referring to the handout labeled “Materials for Briefing on Governance Issues Associated with Liftoff.”	96	9
201504	265	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	When you commence the normalization process, the Committee will set the stance of policy by announcing the new target range for the federal funds rate.	96	9
201504	266	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	In addition, as you’ve discussed previously, the Committee and Board will set the administered rates—the IOER rate will be set to the top of the new target range and the ON RRP rate will be set to the bottom of the new target range.	96	9
201504	267	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The Federal Reserve will also announce the details associated with the capacity of the ON RRP facility and the discount rate, which will be set at a spread above the top of the federal funds rate target range.	96	9
201504	268	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Earlier this month, you received a memo outlining possible arrangements for enhanced reporting of market developments and the governance of decisions on operational adjustments to the administered rates around the time of liftoff.	96	9
201504	269	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	In the early days after the liftoff announcement, it may be somewhat difficult to get a clear picture of how normalization is proceeding because it may take several days for some participants in money markets to adapt to the new market environment.	96	9
201504	270	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	For example, money market participants may need to revise investment guidelines, counterparty limits, or other restrictions on their allocation of funds so that they are able to engage in the arbitrage opportunities available after liftoff.	96	9
201504	271	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Even if the federal funds rate initially lies below the Committee’s new target range, you may judge that the prudent course is to monitor developments while giving money markets some time to adjust.	96	9
201504	272	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	During these early days, you may find it useful to prearrange briefings during which the staff could provide updates on market developments and assess the effectiveness of policy implementation, and you could ask questions.	96	9
201504	273	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	For example, you could schedule daily briefings for perhaps the first two weeks following the liftoff announcement; such briefings could be held via audio or videoconference.	96	9
201504	274	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	These briefings would not be FOMC meetings, so no transcripts or minutes would be prepared.	96	9
201504	275	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Should you wish to express your views about market developments or discuss whether to adjust the target range or the administered rates, the briefings could be readily converted into joint meetings of the Committee and Board.	96	9
201504	276	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	If the liftoff process does not proceed as planned and the funds rate is persistently outside its new target range, then you would presumably wish to discuss the timing and course of possible policy actions, and the scheduled briefings would be replaced by joint videoconference meetings.	96	9
201504	277	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	As discussed in the memo we sent you, the FOMC and Board may also wish to establish decisionmaking procedures that would govern small operational adjustments to the administered rates after the first two weeks or so following the liftoff announcement.	96	9
201504	278	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Adjustments to these administered rates could be helpful if the effective federal funds rate were persistently outside its new target range.	96	9
201504	279	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The memo did not discuss the advantages or disadvantages associated with adjusting the IOER and ON RRP rates, either separately or together, relative to the new target range for the federal funds rate.	96	9
201504	280	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The memo focused on the governance of any such adjustments, and we provided two approaches for you to consider.	96	9
201504	281	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Under the first approach, each adjustment would be approved by a vote of the Committee or Board.	96	9
201504	282	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The Chair could convene a joint FOMC and Board meeting via videoconference at which you could discuss potential changes to the administered rates; all policymakers would be involved in the discussion of changes to the IOER and ON RRP rates.	96	9
201504	283	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Following that discussion, the FOMC would vote on any change to the ON RRP rate, while the Board would approve any change to the IOER rate.	96	9
201504	284	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	A variation on this approach would involve policymakers using SDS to submit comments on proposed adjustments to one or both of the administered rates, with approvals for changes to the ON RRP rate and/or IOER rate recorded via notation votes by the FOMC and Board, respectively.	96	9
201504	285	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	While this would be operationally less burdensome than holding a meeting, and would not require the preparation of transcripts and minutes, it would not allow for an interactive discussion and, as a result, might be most appropriate for relatively straightforward adjustments that the Committee had previously discussed.	96	9
201504	286	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Under the second approach, you would delegate to the Chair authority to adjust the ON RRP and IOER rates, subject to limitations established by the FOMC and Board.	96	9
201504	287	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	If the first couple of weeks of the normalization process had proceeded smoothly and you felt comfortable with the delegation approach, one of the staff briefings could be converted to a meeting at which you would formally take the decision to delegate authority.	96	9
201504	288	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	You might prefer this approach to ensure that the Federal Reserve is able to respond quickly should market conditions warrant.	96	9
201504	289	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	This delegation would allow the Chair to make small adjustments to the administered rates if deemed necessary to keep the federal funds rate trading in its new target range.	96	9
201504	290	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	As an example, the memo suggested that the Chair could be authorized to make adjustments of perhaps 5 or 10 basis points in the administered rates and also indicated that policymakers could determine in advance whether they preferred to address such a situation by adjusting the IOER rate, the ON RRP rate, or both rates in parallel in order to maintain a constant spread between them.	96	9
201504	291	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	There may be some communications advantages associated with the delegation scenario in that it would clearly separate your decisions on the stance of policy—the target range for the federal funds rate established by the FOMC—from small technical adjustments to the administered rates necessary to achieve that policy stance.	96	9
201504	292	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The final page of your handout lists the questions that were distributed with the memo for today’s go-round on governance issues.	96	9
201504	293	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Another memo that was distributed at the same time concerned the setting of the primary credit rate.	96	9
201504	294	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The lending rate for primary credit was originally set in 2003 at 100 basis points above the Committee’s target for the federal funds rate.	96	9
201504	295	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The spread was reduced twice during the financial crisis, and has stood 50 basis points above the top of the federal funds rate target range since February 2010.	96	9
201504	296	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	The memo discussed two options for the setting of the primary credit rate spread:  maintaining that spread at 50 basis points above the top of the Committee’s new funds rate target range at the time of liftoff and for some period thereafter, or raising the spread to 100 basis points at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201504	297	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	During the go-round, you may also wish to share any views you might have on that issue.	96	9
201504	298	2015-04-29	meeting	MEADE	Thank you; this concludes my prepared remarks.	96	9
201504	299	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	300	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Before we turn to questions for Ellen and our go-round, I would like to just make a few remarks of my own.	96	9
201504	301	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	At the outset, I want to emphasize that although our policy tools, by law, have different governance structures, the overall conduct of monetary policy is obviously the purview of the FOMC.	96	9
201504	302	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	The governance issues before us this morning really don’t concern the determination of our intended stance of monetary policy.	96	9
201504	303	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Rather, this discussion pertains to the narrow issue of how to make tactical adjustments to our policy tools to deliver the intended stance of policy.	96	9
201504	304	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	We have spent a great deal of time and effort in devising our framework for normalization, and I am highly confident that it will work.	96	9
201504	305	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	But it is clear that when the time comes to raise the federal funds rate, we will face unprecedented uncertainties, and we need to stand ready to make adjustments, if needed.	96	9
201504	306	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	It is important that we agree on an approach for managing both the initial phase of liftoff and the process for subsequent adjustments that may conceivably be needed once that initial phase is complete.	96	9
201504	307	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	The staff memo proposed that, for the first two weeks or so after liftoff, we set aside time on our calendars to receive frequent market updates and, if necessary, hold meetings to make adjustments to our tools through the Committee and Board votes.	96	9
201504	308	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	During this time, the FOMC may need to reconsider the setting of our tools, including the administered rates, parameters of the overnight RRP facility, and the use of term tools.	96	9
201504	309	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	I just want to make clear that, in my own view, decisions during this initial period should not be delegated to me.	96	9
201504	310	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	The FOMC and Board should vote on adjustments that are deemed necessary after debating the relevant policy considerations and alternative approaches.	96	9
201504	311	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	For example, if the funds rate is trading soft relative to the target range, the Committee should decide whether to raise both rates, keeping the IOER‒ON RRP spread constant, or to instead adjust only one of the rates.	96	9
201504	312	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	These decisions are not entirely tactical or routine.	96	9
201504	313	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	My expectation, however, is that after some initial period, which the memo is guessing might be two weeks, we will have a reasonably good sense regarding how our approach is working, and only minor adjustments, if any, might be subsequently needed to keep the federal funds rate in the target range.	96	9
201504	314	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Assuming that our approach works roughly as expected, such intensive monitoring on the part of the Committee shouldn’t be necessary beyond this initial phase.	96	9
201504	315	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	We ought to be able to settle into an arrangement in which, at most, modest adjustment to our tools, especially to the administered rates, will be called for to keep the federal funds rate in the target range.	96	9

201504	498	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a result, I could imagine a wide variety of adjustments that may be necessary following liftoff.	96	9
201504	499	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While the federal funds rate and other short-term rates may be comfortably bounded by the IOER and overnight RRP rates, I can easily imagine situations in which that is not the case.	96	9
201504	500	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I can also imagine circumstances in which some market rates do not adjust as expected to changes in our policy rates.	96	9
201504	501	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition, it is difficult to predict how variable policy or market rates will be at liftoff.	96	9
201504	502	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	My preferred approach, in light of my concerns, would be to have frequent briefings, initially following liftoff, along with the flexibility to turn those into joint FOMC‒Board meetings, if necessary.	96	9
201504	503	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Once the relationship of the funds rate and other market rates to our tools, as well as the variability of those rates, is better understood, we could agree on the appropriate delegation of tactical decisions to the Chair.	96	9
201504	504	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Predetermining our arrangements for delegation at this time serves little purpose, if they are quite likely to change after liftoff.	96	9
201504	505	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I recommend being humble about how much we know now about liftoff and plan appropriately to have significant consultation and adjustments as we develop a more practical understanding of the challenges of lifting interest rates from the zero lower bound.	96	9
201504	506	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, it is probably premature to determine the normal relationship we expect for the primary credit rate.	96	9
201504	507	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The current spread of 50 basis points above the IOER rate seems an appropriate spread at liftoff.	96	9
201504	508	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	We can decide to alter the spread once it is clear where the federal funds rate and other short-term rates are likely to trade relative to our policy tools.	96	9
201504	509	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In summary, I suggest a highly flexible policy that is highly consultative.	96	9
201504	510	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Once relationships are better understood after liftoff, we can discuss delegation of tactical decisions for achieving our goals.	96	9
201504	511	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	512	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	513	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Mester.	96	9
201504	514	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	515	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	I am comfortable with a governance approach that involves prescheduled staff briefings for a period of time after liftoff and then, after the initial period when things appear to have settled down, delegating authority to the Chair to make small technical adjustments to the ON RRP and IOER rates between FOMC meetings.	96	9
201504	516	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	These technical adjustments would be for the purpose of keeping the funds rate from moving persistently outside the FOMC’s target range.	96	9
201504	517	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	If the Committee agrees on the delegation governance structure, then this delegation of authority should be communicated at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201504	518	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	It is important that the Committee be aware of the developments in financial markets and the effectiveness of policy implementation after the liftoff announcement, and the briefings would be very useful in that regard.	96	9
201504	519	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Whether two weeks is the appropriate time for the initial period isn’t clear to me at this point.	96	9
201504	520	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	If we opt to prearrange daily briefings for two weeks, we might also prearrange a weekly briefing for the remainder of the intermeeting period.	96	9
201504	521	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Of course, the briefings could be converted to meetings, if necessary.	96	9
201504	522	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	I do believe it is important that we demonstrate after liftoff that we have the tools to bring the federal funds rate into our target range.	96	9
201504	523	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	That may necessitate making modest changes in the ON RRP rate or IOER rate in a nimble way.	96	9
201504	524	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Delegating the decisions for these technical changes to the Chair seems appropriate.	96	9
201504	525	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	I believe we should treat the IOER rate and the ON RRP rate symmetrically with respect to delegation.	96	9
201504	526	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	That is, if we delegate to the Chair, we should delegate the authority to make technical changes in both rates.	96	9
201504	527	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Changes that are strategic policy decisions should remain under the purview of the full Committee.	96	9
201504	528	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	These would include decisions to deploy the auxiliary policy tools, like term deposits and term RRPs, as well as making larger changes in the IOER and RRP rates and, of course, changes in the federal funds rate target.	96	9
201504	529	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Particularly if liftoff doesn’t go as planned and the funds rate is trading persistently outside its target range, the full Committee needs to be responsible for making those hard choices and helping to communicate them to the public.	96	9
201504	530	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	The Chair shouldn’t have to go it alone.	96	9
201504	531	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	The Committee hasn’t had a full discussion of what constitutes successful liftoff.	96	9
201504	532	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	This will help inform whether a technical adjustment is needed.	96	9
201504	533	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Let me offer the view that liftoff will be successful if the federal funds rate is within the target range on most, but not necessarily all, days.	96	9
201504	534	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	In my view, successful liftoff does not require that the funds rate be at the midpoint of the range.	96	9
201504	535	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	We plan to operate with a target range of 25 basis points because we don’t expect to have precise control over the funds rate.	96	9
201504	536	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Under those conditions, I don’t think we should require the funds rate to be close to the midpoint of the range.	96	9
201504	537	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Communication of any technical adjustments is an issue.	96	9
201504	538	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	We have indicated to the public that at liftoff we will continue to target a range for the funds rate that is 25 basis points wide and set the IOER and ON RRP rates at the upper and lower bounds of the funds rate target range, respectively.	96	9
201504	539	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	If we find that adjustments are necessary to keep the funds rate in the target range, we must depart from these plans in one way or another.	96	9
201504	540	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Presumably, this can better be handled if, at the time of liftoff, we acknowledge to the public that technical adjustments to the two rates might be necessary and that, as we proceed with liftoff and normalization, the Board of Governors and FOMC have delegated authority to the Chair to make those adjustments, and also that any technical adjustments would not constitute a change in policy.	96	9
201504	541	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	542	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	543	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	96	9
201504	544	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	545	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I am comfortable prescheduling the staff briefings during the first few weeks following liftoff.	96	9
201504	546	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	They can be canceled if they are not needed—all is working smoothly, for example, and the federal funds rate is trading within its target range—or they could be converted to joint FOMC‒Board meetings if adjustments to the overnight RRP and IOER rates are needed to keep the federal funds rate in its target range.	96	9
201504	547	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Obviously, we have to retain some flexibility about how long this period lasts, depending on what our experience is.	96	9
201504	548	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Turning to the governance approach beyond this initial period, I very much favor distinguishing between changes that are tactical, such as small shifts in the overnight RRP rate and the IOER rate to achieve the federal funds rate target selected by the Committee and changes in policy, which are shifts in the target federal funds rate—this goes to President George’s question.	96	9
201504	549	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there is a long history that tactical changes needed to implement the monetary policy stance that has been selected by the Committee can and should be delegated either to the Chair or to the Desk.	96	9
201504	550	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If you consider how policy was implemented prior to the crisis, the Desk, in close consultation with Board staff, decided how much in reserves to add or drain each day in order to keep the federal funds rate close to its target.	96	9
201504	551	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	For many years, presumably as a governance measure, there was also one FOMC member on the call, essentially to keep an eye on the proceedings.	96	9
201504	552	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The decision on the amount of intervention and the means of intervention was left during normal times to the staff, the New York Desk, and the Division of Monetary Affairs at the Board.	96	9
201504	553	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In unusual circumstances—for example, August 2007—the staff consulted closely with the Chair in making those reserve adjustment decisions.	96	9
201504	554	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The issue in my mind is whether changes in the overnight RRP and the IOER rates that are small and designed to keep the federal funds rate in its target range meet this tactical criteria, and I think they do.	96	9
201504	555	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The changes contemplated would be to implement the monetary policy stance that had already been mandated by the Committee.	96	9
201504	556	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So this argues for delegation.	96	9
201504	557	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	One could even argue for delegation to the Desk and the Division of Monetary Affairs staff, but I don’t see any reason to go this far.	96	9
201504	558	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I would favor delegating it to the Chair to make clear that it is receiving the attention it deserves by senior policymakers.	96	9
201504	559	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, delegation to the Chair might be more appropriate in this particular case, because such decisions are about the level of interest rates offered on our facilities rather than as in the past, on the amount of reserves we might add or drain.	96	9
201504	560	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	To implement this after the initial period, I would give the Chair the discretion to move the overnight RRP rate up or down by as much as 10 basis points, so a range of 20 basis points, and the IOER rate up or down by as much as 10 basis points as needed to keep the funds rate within its target range.	96	9
201504	561	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The adjustments could either be in tandem to maintain a constant spread, or the spread could be widened or narrowed subject to those criteria.	96	9
201504	562	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In contrast to the delegation of modest IOER and overnight RRP rate changes to the Chair, I think any other changes—such as implementing the time deposit facility and things like that or changing the size of the cap on the overnight RRP facility—should be left to the full Committee.	96	9
201504	563	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the overnight RRP cap, this is pretty consequential because it will affect the composition of money market flows, and also it is unlikely that changes in the overnight RRP cap are going to be needed on a day-by-day basis.	96	9
201504	564	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So having the Committee make these changes is not going to be particularly arduous; they will probably be made on a much more irregular basis, if at all.	96	9
201504	565	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	566	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	567	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	96	9
201504	568	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	569	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Yes, I’m comfortable scheduling a bunch of briefings that can be converted at short notice to meetings.	96	9
201504	570	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I think that adjustment of the IOER or the overnight RRP rates in the first few weeks following liftoff should clearly require an FOMC meeting.	96	9
201504	571	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I would point out that it took us almost a year to figure out how we wanted to set the IOER and the overnight RRP rates relative to the funds rate.	96	9
201504	572	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Committee members brought different considerations to the tradeoffs involved, and the initial settings involve a compromise among different views about those tradeoffs.	96	9
201504	573	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	New information about performance of those settings after liftoff is likely to inform Committee members’ views about those tradeoffs and likely require recalibration of that compromise.	96	9
201504	574	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	For me, it’s hard to imagine a routine adjustment.	96	9
201504	575	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	The analogy has been drawn to the Desk’s draining and adding reserves through open market operations.	96	9
201504	576	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I’d point out that it has taken decades for those to become as routine as they did.	96	9
201504	577	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	And at times when the FOMC has changed its operational regime, those things have been tricky at first, and the Committee has likely, in many of those instances, been very involved.	96	9
201504	578	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m thinking about the early 1980s and times in the 1970s, when the instructions to the Desk were very different.	96	9
201504	579	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It’s going to take a while for changes to the IOER or overnight RRP rates to be seen as routine or technical rather than something like: “All right, we’ve set up a new regime, we’re trying to calibrate the settings of these things,” and the Committee needs to be involved.	96	9
201504	580	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	What I’d advocate is that we plan to make all the decisions at meetings until the first meeting at which a decision that is made appears, in hindsight, to have been clearly routine; from then on we can delegate the routine of changing it.	96	9
201504	581	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think routine changes are likely, to my mind.	96	9
201504	582	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	If you think about it, what’s at stake here is the spread: the arbitrage margin between the funds market and the IOER rate.	96	9
201504	583	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It seems like 20 basis points, 15 basis points, somewhere in there.	96	9
201504	584	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	That doesn’t seem like something that’s likely to fluctuate the way the need for adding or draining reserves fluctuated on a daily basis.	96	9
201504	585	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	If it fluctuates, that’s big news if it goes to 30 or 40 basis points.	96	9
201504	586	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I’d be kind of surprised about that, and I think we’d want to get to the bottom of it.	96	9
201504	587	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think we have an understanding of those markets in which it looks like, yes, they should routinely fluctuate by 10 or 20 basis points.	96	9
201504	588	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I’d urge us just to plan on making these decisions at meetings.	96	9
201504	589	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m happy to delegate if it comes to pass that these turn out to be routine decisions that the Committee feels like delegating.	96	9
201504	590	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Let’s go and make one of those decisions at a time like that and then delegate thereafter.	96	9
201504	591	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I also wanted to talk about the discount rate spread.	96	9
201504	592	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	The discount rate spread is 50 basis points, and it’s irrelevant to monetary policy right now in the sense that it doesn’t limit spikes in the federal funds rate when reserve supply is unexpectedly shortened.	96	9
201504	593	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It’s not going to be relevant to monetary policy implementation in that sense until—2020, I think, is the latest staff projection.	96	9
201504	594	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Its relevance now is basically for small banks that come up short on reserves due to poor planning or some unforeseeable contingency that they could claim is outside their control but probably isn’t.	96	9
201504	595	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Now, large banks have a ton of reserves that insulate them against shocks, and they don’t come to the window.	96	9
201504	596	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Right now, in our current situation of large reserve balances, this is basically about giving the incentive to small banks to manage their accounts sensibly.	96	9
201504	597	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I think our old normal spread of 100 basis points would provide a more appropriate incentive, given the amounts of money involved if you actually do the overnight calculation.	96	9
201504	598	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I think we should move back to 100 when we lift off.	96	9
201504	599	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I would favor that.	96	9
201504	600	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It was there.	96	9
201504	601	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	We set that in 2002.	96	9
201504	602	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	We did some analysis.	96	9
201504	603	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	There was some thought given to the tradeoff involved.	96	9
201504	604	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I think it makes sense.	96	9
201504	605	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It would also signal normalization in a way that would be useful.	96	9
201504	606	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	When you talk about discount window borrowing, the word “stigma” inevitably comes up, and the idea is advanced that, well, keeping the primary credit rate low helps reduce stigma.	96	9
201504	607	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	That is certainly true in the only model we have of stigma and discount window lending, but the survey research we’ve done as part of the a group looking at discount window issues—they did some survey work on stigma, and what they found is that it is not a relevant consideration for small banks.	96	9
201504	608	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Small banks don’t feel stigmatized.	96	9
201504	609	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Maybe they feel stigmatized already, but they don’t feel as if stigma inhibits their borrowing from the window.	96	9
201504	610	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It’s just a big bank or a too- big-to-fail bank kind of issue, and large banks don’t borrow now.	96	9
201504	611	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	In the last crisis, we lowered the primary credit rate when it looked as if there was a rationale for big banks borrowing at the window.	96	9
201504	612	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	It turned out they were getting all of the money they needed from Federal Home Loan Banks anyway, so it didn’t seem to be particularly relevant to large banks either.	96	9
201504	613	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think stigma is a reason to keep the discount rate spread at 50 basis point rather than 100.	96	9
201504	614	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	That’s the import of that.	96	9
201504	615	2015-04-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201504	647	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	648	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	First, with respect to the meetings and briefings, I guess I’m having trouble seeing what the utility of daily briefings for a couple of weeks would be in the circumstance that we think is likely to obtain, which is that there’s a reasonably successful liftoff.	96	9

201504	650	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thereafter, I’m just not sure how much there will be to say unless things are going wrong, in which case, as everybody says, we’re going to actually need meetings and not just briefings.	96	9
201504	651	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I just note that in passing.	96	9
201504	652	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I know this Committee can fill up virtually any meeting that is set with questions and conversation, but I’m just not sure how much there will be to say other than getting emails from Simon and Lorie telling us what has happened on day three.	96	9
201504	653	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to governance, like everybody, I think, who’s spoken on this point, I favor giving discretion to the Chair, but actually I think I would go further than the staff though.	96	9
201504	654	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Indeed, I’m going to disagree with the Chair in the interest of giving her more discretion than she asked for.	96	9
201504	655	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I guess I don’t quite understand why we wouldn’t give her discretion for this kind of modest change in the IOER rate or the ON RRP rate or both, even in the immediate post-liftoff period.	96	9
201504	656	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	It is new, but we have spent most of the past year talking about how important it is to have a smooth and credible liftoff.	96	9
201504	657	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	And, notwithstanding my substantial uneasiness with the potential medium-term effects of a large ON RRP facility, I’ve joined the consensus that our dominant goal should be that smooth and credible liftoff, and presumably that smoothness and credibility are going to be most important in the immediate post-liftoff period, which is to say the first couple of days.	96	9
201504	658	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	It seems to me that if we regard the adjustments as fine-tuning in pursuit of a particular federal funds target rate range, it would be useful to give her the discretion in that first couple of days to make such adjustments in an effort to get, as Loretta says, to at least the bottom of that range.	96	9
201504	659	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	If there’s a major problem with liftoff, we’re going to need another full FOMC meeting.	96	9
201504	660	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	But suppose, for example, there’s a little bit of softness in the floor on the first day or two after the announced liftoff, and that softness might be firmed by a modest adjustment in the IOER rate.	96	9
201504	661	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	A quick action of that sort might actually buttress the credibility of our tools and intentions right from the outset and thereby make the whole process smoother.	96	9
201504	662	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think, in any case, it represents a policy change, because we can talk about it beforehand.	96	9
201504	663	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Now, it’s possible that markets might read such a quick adjustment as indicating that we lack confidence in the efficacy of the decision we had just made a day or two before.	96	9
201504	664	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	But that’s a judgment that the Chair could make in consultation with those best able to discern what market sentiment and intentions may be.	96	9
201504	665	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Just by indicating that nimbleness is a desideratum, I think I’ve already explained why an FOMC decisionmaking process won’t do the trick.	96	9
201504	666	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I just think the logic of what we’re talking about here argues for giving the Chair this kind of very limited discretion to adjust those two rates that we’ve been talking about and we will set at the time of liftoff in the period in which they might be most efficacious in changing or shaping perceptions of how this whole process is going to go.	96	9
201504	667	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	As to communication, it does seem to me proper to indicate in advance that small, operational adjustments might be made in the IOER and ON RRP rates between meetings.	96	9
201504	668	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Characterizing those as operational adjustments beforehand and contemplating them, I think, helps reinforce the sense that these are technical changes rather than policy changes.	96	9
201504	669	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	The suggestion that any actual changes be noted by the Desk, as opposed to the Chair or the Committee as a whole, also seems to me a good idea since it would reinforce the fact that these rates are more or less operational changes rather than policy changes.	96	9
201504	670	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	On the primary credit rate spread, I thought President Lacker’s comments were very interesting.	96	9
201504	671	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Notwithstanding the fact that they are interesting and we should think about them, particularly this difference between small and large bank stigma when we do discuss this, I personally would prefer to wait until the staff thinking about stigma effects and perhaps other elements of the discount window are done and maybe a more fulsome memo has been produced and circulated so that we can have a discussion of that.	96	9
201504	672	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	It seems to me we’ve got plenty on our plate right now, and we might usefully put that conversation off just a bit.	96	9
201504	673	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I want to end by saying I hadn’t thought about it this way, but I fully endorse what Loretta said about the criteria for success in how we regard the meeting of the target range post- liftoff, and I think if we all subscribe to that, it would be useful for us, through appropriate mechanisms, to get that expectation out as well so that we’re being evaluated by commentators and markets in a manner consistent with what our actual intentions and aims are.	96	9
201504	674	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Like President Mester, again, this is another reason why I think these little adjustments even right after liftoff are fine for the Chair to make.	96	9
201504	675	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	And, like President Mester, I think using any of the other tools is something that should involve the entire Committee.	96	9
201504	676	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201504	684	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	I feel that in the days after liftoff, if things are not going exactly as we intend, and the funds rate is drifting outside the range, I do really think it’s appropriate for the entire Committee to meet, discuss what is happening, try to get to the bottom of what the problem is, and decide on what the approach is.	96	9
201504	685	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Now, we could make the decision that this is no big deal, the funds rate is just fluctuating around relative to the target range by more than we had anticipated and this is the “new normal.”	96	9
