201504	693	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	If it should turn out that between the regularly scheduled FOMC meetings the funds rate begins to trade frequently below the overnight reverse repo rate for a reasonably sized ON RRP facility, I support the Chair having limited discretionary authority to restore funds rate control by raising both the IOER and the ON RRP rates while maintaining the spread between the two rates.	96	9
201504	694	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	I agree with Governor Tarullo that this could be within the first days as well.	96	9
201504	695	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	That these rate changes are not to be subject to a vote would signal that they are technical adjustments designed simply to implement previously- agreed-upon policy.	96	9
201504	696	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	The main focus would stay on the target band for the federal funds rate set by the FOMC.	96	9
201504	697	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	The simplicity of a system in which the IOER and the ON RRP rates are set equal to the top and bottom of the target funds rate band, respectively, is appealing and easily communicated.	96	9
201504	698	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	Deviations from that simple system should be temporary with reserve-draining tools, like term deposits and term RRPs, being brought to bear when systematically greater interest rate control is required.	96	9
201504	699	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	I understand that we are entering uncharted territory and may need to act nimbly.	96	9
201504	700	2015-04-29	meeting	HOLCOMB	Therefore, a good solution is for the FOMC and the Board to give the Chair discretionary authority to adjust the IOER–ON RRP band relative to the funds rate target range between meetings while maintaining the width of the band at 25 basis points.	96	9

201504	825	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee insists on saying that the federal funds rate is the policy rate, but relatively few trades are occurring at that particular rate.	96	9
201504	826	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	According to the Committee, the IOER rate is not the policy rate, but, on the other hand, that is the rate that affects the largest banks in the country, and it affects their funding costs.	96	9
201504	827	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	And, in other contexts, we have said IOER is our workhorse rate.	96	9
201504	828	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	And then you’ve got overnight RRP, which we’re also saying is not a policy rate, but which is for a market that has many traders and that is potentially large at the time of liftoff.	96	9
201504	829	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	So we might say that the policy rate is the federal funds rate, but what does that mean to markets?	96	9
201504	830	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	It’s really the markets that are saying what the policy rate is, and if they think moving these other rates is more important than where the federal funds rate is trading, then we’ve changed policy in a macroeconomic sense.	96	9
201504	831	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	So, I think this is a conflict, but that is part of the situation we’re in, given the way we’ve decided to do this.	96	9
201504	832	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think it does have potential to sound like a policy move to people inside financial markets even though we’re saying, well, the federal funds rate range has not changed and so we haven’t done anything different.	96	9
201504	833	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	The bottom line is that I am worried about communications issues.	96	9
201504	834	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Because of that, I don’t think you want to do this unless it’s absolutely necessary.	96	9
201504	835	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	You know, overall I would say 5 to 10 basis points per intermeeting period is okay with me.	96	9
201504	836	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	I would agree with President Rosengren that it might be premature to decide on this today.	96	9
201504	837	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	You could make the delegation decision later around the time of liftoff, if necessary.	96	9
201504	838	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Let me finish with one story that old-timers here around the Federal Reserve will remember from the early 1990s.	96	9
201504	839	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	I am going to mention “He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named,” who is former Chairman Alan Greenspan.	96	9
201504	840	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	At the time, it was considered that the Chairman had 25 basis points on the federal funds rate target and that the Chairman could make that adjustment during an intermeeting period without consulting the Committee.	96	9
201504	841	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	And the Chairman at that time made a bunch of those moves and then came into the meeting and said, “Now that I’ve made the move, now we don’t have to move at the meeting.”	96	9
201504	842	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	This was extremely hot and divisive on the Committee in the early 1990s.	96	9
201504	843	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	We don’t want to get into any kind of situation like that, and I know that’s not your intention, but it is a bit of a slippery slope:  What’s going to be delegated?	96	9
201504	844	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Who’s agreed to it?	96	9
201504	845	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	How much have you agreed to?	96	9
201504	846	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Under what circumstances?	96	9
201504	847	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	It is a very tricky issue, and it has been a situation in the past on this Committee that has been problematic from a collegiality perspective.	96	9
201504	848	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	I know we’re not really thinking about anything like that, but I think it is a bit of a slippery slope.	96	9
201504	849	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	You’ve got this issue about what rates really matter versus what rates we are calling the policy rate, and you’ve got this precedent in the past when it didn’t go so well.	96	9
201504	850	2015-04-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	851	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	96	9
201504	852	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Fischer.	96	9
201504	853	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9
201504	854	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’m comfortable with the governance approach in the first two weeks of scheduling daily staff briefings, but I assume that we’ll quickly work out whether we need them every day and we can probably unschedule a few of them within a day or two.	96	9
201504	855	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	So I think there’s some flexibility there.	96	9
201504	856	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	With regard to the governance approach for technical adjustments in the IOER or ON RRP rates, I don’t know about previous Chairmen.	96	9
201504	857	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’ve only had one Chair in my life on the Board, and my experience with that Chair is that if there is going to be any question about a need for discussion, she will call for it.	96	9
201504	858	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I haven’t detected her trying to get around the FOMC or the Board, and I think we can rely on that.	96	9
201504	859	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	So I’d be perfectly willing to give the Chair an adjustment up to 10 basis points.	96	9
201504	860	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I agree that we need to specify that the discretion would be granted between meetings.	96	9
201504	861	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’m not sure about the wisdom of constraining the gap between the ON RRP and IOER rates to 25 basis points.	96	9
201504	862	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	We may find reasons why we need to move one without moving the other, and my general approach is, don’t constrain yourself if there’s no need to constrain yourself, because the law of unintended consequences is very powerful.	96	9
201504	863	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	On the primary credit rate, I agree with those who think we should try to minimize the number of adjustments we make at the time of liftoff, and that this issue is sufficiently important for banks to which we give a lot more attention than their size would imply.	96	9
201504	864	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’m not sure why we would want to start by raising the cost of borrowing by 50 basis points for the smaller banks who do borrow at that rate, and we’d need to look at what would happen when we raise the rate.	96	9
201504	865	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	And so, for both reasons, I favor examining that after liftoff.	96	9
201504	866	2015-04-29	meeting	FISCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	96	9

201504	871	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	As for the briefings, I think it is fine to schedule them, and if we have them I’ll attend them, but I think the only case in which we would actually want to have them is if things are really not going well.	96	9
201504	872	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	And I don’t expect that that is likely at all in a world in which we have taken the cap off the overnight RRP or, for that matter, put a very high cap on.	96	9
201504	873	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	As far as delegation is concerned, if the test is adjustments that are routine or technical in nature, I completely trust the Chair’s instincts on that.	96	9
201504	874	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	I will say that if what we’re dealing with is a very difficult and failed liftoff situation, I don’t think, in real time, that’s going to feel either routine or technical.	96	9

201504	878	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	So, for all of that, I think it’s essentially impossible to anticipate all of these things, and I would just say that I will do what is reasonable at the time.	96	9
201504	879	2015-04-29	meeting	POWELL	In terms of the primary credit facility, it is an interesting subject on which we can have a lot of debate.	96	9

201504	887	2015-04-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I think it’s very important for us as Committee members to take responsibility for actively being engaged in assessing the effectiveness of monetary control and the relative roles of the IOER and the ON RRP rates in maintaining the federal funds rate in the target range for some initial period.	96	9

201504	890	2015-04-29	meeting	BRAINARD	When market functioning has settled down, it will be appropriate to delegate to the Chair the authority to make the necessary changes to the levels of the IOER and the ON RRP rates, or possibly to the spread between them, in order to maintain effective monetary control.	96	9

201504	894	2015-04-29	meeting	BRAINARD	But like many others around the table, I would want to put some distance between the timing of liftoff and the timing of possibly changing that spread so as not to further complicate our already challenging communications around the time of liftoff.	96	9

201504	901	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	11	1
201504	902	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	I’ll be referring to the top exhibit on your pile, which is labeled “Material for the US Outlook.”	11	1
201504	903	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The data on spending, production, and hiring that we received since the March Tealbook were all weaker than we expected.	11	1
201504	904	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	On the spending side, the February PCE data and March retail sales report led us to make a sizable reduction in our estimate of first-quarter real PCE growth.	11	1
201504	905	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	This downward revision to consumer spending accounts for much of the downward revision to first-quarter real GDP growth shown in panel 1 of your forecast summary exhibit.	11	1
201504	906	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In addition, a number of other categories of spending— particularly business investment and residential construction—have also surprised us to the downside in recent months, as have the incoming data on factory output.	11	1
201504	907	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	I would note that after the April Tealbook was closed, we received the advance report on capital goods orders and shipments for March, which was also weak but broadly in line with our expectations.	11	1
201504	908	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	One of the crucial questions that we faced—and that you face as well—was how to interpret this batch of disappointing news, and whether, in particular, it is best seen as just another hiccup in a recovery that fundamentally remains on track toward achievement of your policy objectives, or the leading edge of a more serious slackening in the pace of recovery.	11	1
201504	909	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	For the most part, we have leaned toward the former interpretation.	11	1
201504	910	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Accordingly, our projection calls for near-term real GDP growth to return to a pace that is not too different from our March forecast.	11	1
201504	911	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In particular, although it is difficult to quantify their influence precisely, we believe that several transitory special factors—including unusually severe winter weather and production disruptions related to labor disputes at West Coast ports—were a small drag on first-quarter real activity.	11	1
201504	912	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In addition, we think that measured first-quarter GDP growth will be held down a bit by seasonal adjustment issues that affected estimates of state and local construction spending and by a distortion in the BEA’s translation of retail sales to PCE associated with the steep decline in gasoline prices and the increased share of gasoline sales at large retail establishments such as Wal- Mart.	11	1
201504	913	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	We do not judge any of these factors to be exerting a large influence on their own, but as a group, our back-of-the-envelope calculations put the effect at about ¾ percentage point.	11	1
201504	914	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	That said, we have not completely discounted the weaker-than-expected incoming data.	11	1
201504	915	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Specifically, we trimmed our estimate of consumption growth in the second quarter a bit as a result of the weaker-than-expected March retail sales report, and we made a noticeable downward revision to our projection of near-term residential construction activity in response to the lack of a significant pickup in starts and permits in March.	11	1
201504	916	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	We also lowered our forecast for nonresidential structures spending, as the latest data on drilling activity suggest that the recent drop in oil prices is having a larger effect on drilling and mining investment than we had previously anticipated.	11	1
201504	917	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Because we believe that the fundamentals underpinning household spending remain solid, we continue to expect that real GDP will rise at a pace that exceeds our estimate of potential output growth over the remainder of the year.	11	1
201504	918	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Even so, the level of real output at the end of this year is almost ½ percent lower than in our March forecast.	11	1
201504	919	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	As a way of providing another perspective on the near-term outlook, panel 2 presents the results from the Board staff’s dynamic factor model.	11	1
201504	920	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	This model uses the information from a large number of activity and price indicators to generate forecasts of near-term real GDP growth, and it was among the specifications we showed you in the April Tealbook box on nowcasting models.	11	1
201504	921	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	As you can see, using the data that we had available when the April Tealbook was closed, the model also predicts a very low GDP growth figure for the first quarter followed by a modest pickup in the current quarter.	11	1
201504	922	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Of course, the model does not know about any of the special factors that we think will unwind and provide an additional boost to growth this quarter.	11	1
201504	923	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	And I would note that the range of predictions for first-quarter growth coming from the various nowcasting efforts across the System is quite wide, underscoring the uncertainty surrounding the interpretation of the pace of activity last quarter.	11	1
201504	924	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	To wrap up the discussion of the near-term spending data, I would remind you that we will receive the BEA’s advance estimate of first-quarter real GDP tomorrow morning.	11	1
201504	925	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Given how low our current point estimate is—and in light of the relatively large degree of uncertainty that surrounds these estimates, even on the eve of a release—it would not be especially surprising from a statistical point of view if we were to see either a small decline tomorrow or a noticeably stronger increase than we have penciled in.	11	1
201504	926	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	And, of course, the BEA’s initial estimate is itself subject to substantial revision over time.	11	1
201504	927	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Moving to the middle panels, the labor market has continued to improve, but here, too, the data point to somewhat less momentum than we had anticipated in our previous forecast.	11	1
201504	928	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In the establishment survey, March total nonfarm payroll employment growth was considerably weaker than the very strong pace that we had expected.	11	1
201504	929	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Incorporating revisions to previous months, the average monthly change in payroll employment over the first quarter now stands at about 200,000, which is 70,000 less than we had written down in the March Tealbook.	11	1
201504	930	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The news from the household survey also came in a little weaker than we had anticipated:  The unemployment rate held steady at 5.5 percent in March—we had expected it to tick down one-tenth—while the participation rate, which we had expected to hold steady, edged lower.	11	1
201504	931	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	To summarize the information from the various pieces of labor market data that we have received, panel 3 shows our labor market conditions index, or LMCI.	11	1
201504	932	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	As you can see from the inset box, the LMCI was basically flat last month.	11	1
201504	933	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	For the first quarter as a whole—the rightmost bar in the main chart—the index did increase, but at a slower pace than what we have seen in recent quarters.	11	1
201504	934	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Just as we did with the spending data, we took a modest signal from the incoming labor market news and reduced our projected pace of monthly payroll job growth by about 40,000 over the current quarter.	11	1
201504	935	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	We also nudged up our forecast for the unemployment rate in coming months.	11	1
201504	936	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Over the remainder of the medium term, our projection of real GDP growth is little revised from March.	11	1
201504	937	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The main conditioning factors that we built into the baseline forecast this round—particularly, the lower projected path for the exchange value of the dollar—are, on net, expected to be slightly more supportive of real activity.	11	1
201504	938	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	By the end of the medium term, the effects of these changes offset roughly half of the downward revisions we put through to the near term, leaving the level of real GDP just a little lower relative to our March projection.	11	1
201504	939	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Although it had only a small effect on our projection regarding real activity, I would point out that we now assume that the federal funds rate will lift off from its effective lower bound in September, one quarter later than in our previous forecast.	11	1
201504	940	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Our revised liftoff assumption is broadly consistent with both the “flash” primary dealer survey that was taken after the March FOMC meeting and the latest dealer survey, and it is more consistent with the timing suggested by financial markets.	11	1
201504	941	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In addition, as best we can tell, a September liftoff date does not appear to be sharply at odds with FOMC participants’ March SEP submissions, in which the median participant pointed to the third quarter as the most likely quarter for liftoff.	11	1
201504	942	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	After liftoff—and consistent with our usual practice—the projected path for the funds rate is set by mechanically applying an inertial version of the Taylor (1999) policy rule.	11	1
201504	943	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Panel 4 gives our projected path for the unemployment rate.	11	1
201504	944	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	With the level of real GDP at the end of the medium term only a little lower relative to March—and with no change to our supply-side assumptions this round—the unemployment rate is expected to be 5.1 percent at the end of 2017.	11	1
201504	945	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	This is one-tenth higher than its level in the March Tealbook and one-tenth below our estimate of its natural rate.	11	1
201504	946	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The slow pace of decline in the unemployment rate reflects both the modest pace of GDP growth projected over the medium term and our assumption that the strengthening labor market will draw more individuals back into the labor force.	11	1
201504	947	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Panels 5 and 6 summarize the inflation outlook.	11	1
201504	948	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The incoming data on price inflation have been a touch above our expectations and support our projection that both total and core inflation will step up in the second quarter.	11	1
201504	949	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Further out, the inflation projection is little revised.	11	1
201504	950	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	As in previous Tealbooks, we expect that inflation will gradually move higher as resource slack diminishes, energy prices rise, and prices for imported goods turn up again.	11	1
201504	951	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Finally, I wanted to call your attention to a change we made this round to how we characterize forecast uncertainty in the Tealbook.	11	1
201504	952	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Specifically, we have revamped the methodology that we use to compute confidence intervals based on our historical projection errors and have also reworked our presentation of these intervals to include a comparison with the historical range of key forecast variables.	11	1
201504	953	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	The new intervals are typically a little wider than the ones we reported previously, and they tend to show more asymmetry, which is most noticeable in the prediction interval surrounding the unemployment forecast.	11	1
201504	954	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	When we miss big on unemployment, it tends to be because unemployment turns out to have been much higher than expected, not much lower.	11	1
201504	955	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Additional details on this new methodology were presented in a box and associated technical appendix in the Risks and Uncertainty section of the Tealbook and in Jeremy Nalewaik’s pre-FOMC briefing.	11	1
201504	956	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	These new intervals complement our other methodology of using stochastic simulations from the FRB/US model to produce confidence intervals around our projection, and we intend to show both sets of uncertainty measures in future Tealbooks.	11	1
201504	957	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	I would note that the confidence bands shown in my exhibit today continue to use the FRB/US measures, but our intention is to eventually extend the new methodology to compute confidence intervals around our quarterly forecasts as well.	11	1

201504	959	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Thank you, Bill.	11	1
201504	960	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	The harsh weather we endured last winter left many potholes in US roads and, as Bill Wascher has described, helped create one large pothole in US GDP growth.	11	1
201504	961	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Interestingly, as shown in panel 1 of my presentation on the international outlook, a pothole also appears in the path of foreign growth in the first quarter.	11	1
201504	962	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Incoming data have been surprisingly weak in countries as diverse as Canada, which shared our harsh winter; China, which was actually warmer than usual; and Malaysia, which arguably has no winter at all.	11	1
201504	963	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 2, the downturn was also evident in global trade, suggesting some underlying malaise that was sweeping the globe.	11	1
201504	964	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	As indicated by the yellow bars in panels 1 and 2, we faced a very similar picture exactly a year ago, with US growth, foreign growth, and global trade all turning down in the first quarter of 2014.	11	1
201504	965	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, I went back and looked at my remarks for the April 2014 FOMC meeting for lessons that we might apply here.	11	1
201504	966	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	First, I found that I used the same tired pothole metaphor a year ago.	11	1
201504	967	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	[Laughter]	11	1
201504	968	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Second, at that time, I also predicted that foreign economic activity would clamber out of its pothole and resume moving along the path to recovery, just as Bill Wascher did for the United States.	11	1
201504	969	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Unusually enough, we both turned out to be right, and we are making the same call today.	11	1
201504	970	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Certainly, the fundamentals favor a return to solid growth abroad:  Monetary policy is generally very accommodative, oil prices remain low, and most currencies have weakened considerably against the dollar since last summer.	11	1
201504	971	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Moreover, many of the factors that pushed down global growth in the first quarter appear to be transitory.	11	1
201504	972	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Canada’s economy is estimated to have flatlined on account of unusually harsh winter weather and a step-down in oil investment, but with oil prices bottoming out, growth should bounce back in the coming quarters.	11	1
201504	973	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Mexican output is estimated to have decelerated sharply in the first quarter along with US manufacturing, and we anticipate that the projected rebound in US activity will boost growth in Mexico as well.	11	1
201504	974	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	China also accounts for some of the pothole in foreign growth, but its situation is more complicated.	11	1
201504	975	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 3, GDP growth fell from 7 percent in the fourth quarter to only 5.3 percent in the first, well below expectations, as exports and industrial production dropped sharply.	11	1
201504	976	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	It is difficult to parse out how much of the first-quarter shortfall reflects reduced external demand, how much reflects the ongoing correction in the property sector, and how much reflects longer-term developments such as the rebalancing of the economy and decline in potential output growth.	11	1
201504	977	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	In any event, the authorities had been easing monetary policy even before the weak GDP reading, and they have now stepped up this stimulus, including reducing the required reserve ratio 100 basis points.	11	1
201504	978	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	In our projection, the combination of heightened policy stimulus and rising external demand pushes growth back up to over 7 percent later this year before it edges down thereafter.	11	1
201504	979	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Like the booming Chinese stock market, however, this forecast is somewhat speculative, and we have revised down our projection a bit in response to the recent weakness.	11	1
201504	980	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Ironically, nearly the only bright spot in the global economy has been the euro area, for which strengthening industrial production, retail sales, and PMIs point to a rise in first-quarter GDP growth to 1¾ percent (panel 4).	11	1
201504	981	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Notably, financial conditions are becoming more of a positive for the economy, in part reflecting the ECB’s asset purchase program.	11	1
201504	982	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Bank lending standards are loosening, credit to nonfinancial corporations is finally picking up a bit, interest rates are extremely low, and the real trade-weighted euro is at its weakest level since 2001.	11	1
201504	983	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, we see euro-area growth firming to 2¼ percent in the next few years, provided that spillovers from Greece’s crisis remain contained, as we assume in our baseline.	11	1
201504	984	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	That, however, is a big “if.”	11	1
201504	985	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	The Greek government is struggling in its efforts to negotiate additional financial assistance from European authorities and the IMF, even as it is running arrears to suppliers and raiding the accounts of local governments in order to stay afloat.	11	1
201504	986	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	More than €10 billion in payments on its medium- and long-term debt are coming due in the next four months.	11	1
201504	987	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Although the Greeks have reshuffled their negotiating team in an apparent effort to ease tensions with their creditors and strike a deal, there is still a good chance that the government could miss one or more of these payments.	11	1
201504	988	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Such an event could trigger a run on Greek banks, and unless the ECB stepped up its liquidity support by a substantial margin, the government would have to declare a bank holiday and impose capital controls, with a much-heightened chance of Greece eventually exiting the euro area altogether.	11	1
201504	989	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Had such developments occurred at the height of the euro crisis in 2012, spillovers to the rest of the euro area would have been very destructive.	11	1
201504	990	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	However, as Simon noted, the region’s financial, institutional, and policy framework has strengthened in recent years.	11	1
201504	991	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, we are building into our euro-area forecast only a small drag due to spillovers from Greece’s intensifying crisis.	11	1
201504	992	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Nevertheless, we recognize that, as described in the Tealbook, far more dire scenarios are possible, not just for the euro area but for the global economy more generally.	11	1
201504	993	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	While the pace of economic activity abroad remains quite unsettled, two key external drivers of US economic prospects have been a bit more quiescent of late.	11	1
201504	994	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	First, oil markets have not yielded any big surprises.	11	1
201504	995	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, spot prices, shown in panel 5, are up more than $8 per barrel since the time of the March Tealbook, as falling rig counts and other signs of declining investment have led markets to expect lower US oil production.	11	1
201504	996	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	However, prices for futures contracts further out on the curve are up by less, so that our projected path for Brent prices has been raised just a bit and remains well below levels prevailing last summer.	11	1
201504	997	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Second, for the first time since last July, the dollar has come down over the intermeeting period, as shown in panel 6.	11	1
201504	998	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	This depreciation likely reflected weak data and the fall in expected policy rates here in the United States.	11	1
201504	999	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	However, I would like to remind you that, starting with the March Tealbook, we decided to deviate from our standard random-walk-oriented model and projected a further rise in the dollar.	11	1
201504	1000	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	That also must have contributed to the dollar’s subsequent decline.	11	1
201504	1001	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	[Laughter]	11	1
201504	1002	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	In the event, from its lower starting point, we assume the broad real dollar will still move up some 2¼ percent between now and the end of the year as the US economy bounces back and markets refocus on the policy divergences among major central banks.	11	1
201504	1003	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Your next exhibit puts movements in the dollar and their implications for economic growth into broader perspective.	11	1
201504	1004	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown by the black solid line in panel 1, even at its projected peak early next year, the broad real dollar would be well below its previous two peaks.	11	1
201504	1005	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	The black solid line in panel 2 shows the contribution of net exports to real US GDP growth.	11	1
201504	1006	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	We project it at negative ¾ percentage point this year and next.	11	1
201504	1007	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	This is the largest drag on growth since the early 2000s, and it almost entirely reflects the appreciation of the dollar.	11	1
201504	1008	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	It may seem strange that the dollar should depress the net export contribution to such an extent when it remains so far below its previous peaks.	11	1
201504	1009	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	However, what matters for the contribution of net exports to GDP growth is not the level of the dollar but how much it moves, and the dollar has appreciated sharply since last summer.	11	1
201504	1010	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Additionally, the share of trade in the US economy has grown over time, amplifying the effects of dollar movements on net exports and growth.	11	1
201504	1011	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Were the dollar to rise further than we are currently projecting, it would exert even stronger effects on the economy.	11	1
201504	1012	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Returning to panel 1, the dashed line shows the 10 percent rise in the dollar described in the “Stronger Dollar” scenario in the Tealbook.	11	1
201504	1013	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown below, the contribution of net exports to GDP would fall to its lowest level since the early 1980s.	11	1
201504	1014	2015-04-29	meeting	KAMIN	Additionally, as indicated in panel 3, core inflation would fall below 1 percent on a four-quarter basis before rebounding.	11	1

201504	1016	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Thank you.	FS	FS
201504	1017	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	My material is titled “Financial Stability Developments.”	FS	FS
201504	1018	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	My remarks draw on the recent QS financial stability report.	FS	FS
201504	1019	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In sum, valuation pressures in asset markets have increased since the January assessment and remain notable.	FS	FS
201504	1020	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In addition, vulnerabilities related to maturity and liquidity transformation remain moderate, but leverage in both the financial and the nonfinancial sectors, overall, remains relatively low.	FS	FS
201504	1021	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Taken together, we think that conditions in the financial sector are moderately prone to amplify shocks.	FS	FS
201504	1022	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	I begin with valuations in fixed-income markets.	FS	FS
201504	1023	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The yield on the 10-year Treasury note—the blue line in the upper-left panel—and term premium measures— the red and black lines—have remained quite low since the January financial stability briefing.	FS	FS
201504	1024	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The possibility that term premiums will move up sharply remains a focus of staff analysis.	FS	FS
201504	1025	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	I will return to this issue near the end of the briefing.	FS	FS
201504	1026	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In corporate bond markets, yield spreads to comparable Treasury securities have moved down a bit in recent months.	FS	FS
201504	1027	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As shown by the red line in the panel to the right, the far-term forward spread for high-yield corporate bonds—one measure of risk premiums—remains near the middle of its historical range, which suggests that valuations are reasonable—relative, that is, to seemingly richly valued Treasury securities.	FS	FS
201504	1028	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In addition, as shown by the light blue bars in the middle-left panel, issuance of high-yield bonds, a nonprice measure of hot markets and thus valuation pressures, remained robust through the first quarter of the year.	FS	FS
201504	1029	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Somewhat in contrast, issuance of leveraged loans—the dark blue portion of the bars—has declined, on net, in recent quarters.	FS	FS
201504	1030	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Although supervisory analysis of completed deals suggests a modest improvement in underwriting quality, fairly lax nonprice terms were reportedly still prevalent in recent deals.	FS	FS
201504	1031	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Moving to the stock market, the expected real return on corporate equities—the black line in the middle-right panel—has fallen significantly since the previous stability briefing, as stock prices have advanced and expectations of corporate earnings have been revised down.	FS	FS
201504	1032	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The low expected return suggests that valuations are quite high.	FS	FS
201504	1033	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The equity risk premium, which is the difference between the expected return on stocks and the expected real yield on the 10-year Treasury note, shown in teal, has also moved down sharply, though it remains closer to the middle of its 30-year range.	FS	FS
201504	1034	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Our overall assessment is that equity valuations are somewhat more stretched now than they were just a few months ago.	FS	FS
201504	1035	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	A variety of changes in the structure of fixed-income markets may add to the volatility of interest rates, and, perhaps, to the volatility of volatility.	FS	FS
201504	1036	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	First—and I’m not referring to any panel quite yet—increased electronification of the Treasury market could contribute to occasional and surprising spikes in volatility, such as that which occurred on October 15 of last year.	FS	FS
201504	1037	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In addition, the continued decline in intermediation by dealers—as illustrated by gross and net dealer borrowing, shown in the lower-left panel—is consistent with anecdotes that new regulations have made dealers less willing to provide marketmaking liquidity, even in normal times.	FS	FS
201504	1038	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	A bond market selloff could also be temporarily amplified if investors in bond mutual funds rush for the exits, forcing funds to sell into an illiquid market.	FS	FS
201504	1039	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The rapid growth in assets under management at such funds—shown in the lower-right panel—including funds that hold less-liquid assets, suggests that the scope for such an amplification has increased in recent years.	FS	FS
201504	1040	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The first panel of the next exhibit shows an estimate of the level of “runnable” private money-like instruments.	FS	FS
201504	1041	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	This measure of maturity and liquidity transformation includes cross-holdings of money market instruments, such as when a money fund holds repo.	FS	FS
201504	1042	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	It is therefore an indicator of the vulnerability of the financial system through intermediation chains that rely—at one link or more—on short-term funding.	FS	FS
201504	1043	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The level of these runnables has been fairly stable at a relatively high level during the past two years, as growth in uninsured deposits—the light blue region—has offset a decline in repo—in red—which suggests that the financial system remains moderately vulnerable to runs.	FS	FS
201504	1044	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	A fairly bright—or should I say, green—spot on the financial-stability map is leverage in the banking system.	FS	FS
201504	1045	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As can be seen in the upper-right panel, capital cushions at bank holding companies, as measured by both the Tier 1 common equity ratio—in black—and the leverage ratio—in red—have increased notably.	FS	FS
201504	1046	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	This reflects both Basel III requirements and the resilience required in annual stress tests.	FS	FS
201504	1047	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As you know, no CCAR bank fell below the stress test’s quantitative benchmarks in the most recent round, although three firms had to adjust their planned capital distributions.	FS	FS
201504	1048	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As far as we can tell—which, admittedly, is not very far—leverage in the nonbank financial sector continues to be a vulnerability.	FS	FS
201504	1049	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As summarized in the middle-left panel, overall margin credit has moved down in recent months but remains quite elevated, and hedge funds appear to be using a fairly large amount of portfolio margining from prime brokerages to lever up in equity markets.	FS	FS
201504	1050	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	In addition, responses to the March SCOOS provided some evidence that counterparties have been demanding more leverage to fund non-agency RMBS, high-yield corporate bonds, and securitized CRE loans.	FS	FS
201504	1051	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Unfortunately, leverage embedded in derivatives is hard to measure, so it remains difficult to assess the overall leverage of hedge funds, mutual funds, and other investment vehicles.	FS	FS
201504	1052	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Moving to the private nonfinancial sector, the middle-right panel provides the big picture for households: Modest increases in household debt continue to be driven mostly by prime borrowers—the orange line—though debt of subprime borrowers— the black line—ticked up in the fourth quarter.	FS	FS
201504	1053	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Student loans and subprime auto lending have remained rapid even as delinquencies on these kinds of debt have moved up.	FS	FS
201504	1054	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Although we do not currently consider student and subprime auto debt to be direct vulnerabilities for the financial system, we are alert for potential spillovers to other debt markets.	FS	FS
201504	1055	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As can be seen in the lower-left panel, the debt-to-assets ratio for all nonfinancial corporate businesses—the black line—and for high-yield and unrated firms—the red line—moved up further in the fourth quarter, which suggests a continued buildup of the vulnerability of this sector.	FS	FS
201504	1056	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	The lower-right panel provides a very brief roundup of the potential shocks to the financial system that appear most proximate.	FS	FS
201504	1057	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	A sharp rise in term premiums could precipitate a sudden drop in a variety of asset prices, especially for those with stretched valuations.	FS	FS
201504	1058	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Moreover, for reasons mentioned previously, these shocks could be temporarily amplified if liquidity were to deteriorate just when it is needed most or if bond mutual funds were to experience large and disruptive outflows.	FS	FS
201504	1059	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	That said, the risk of a sustained amplification is mitigated by the apparently modest amount of leverage in the financial system.	FS	FS
201504	1060	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	We are also attuned to the possibility of damaging spillovers from a rate spike here to emerging market economies.	FS	FS
201504	1061	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	As we concluded in a special memo, although blowback to the United States through financial connections would likely be limited, a significant EME recession and a presumed increase in risk aversion would damage the US economy as well.	FS	FS
201504	1062	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	It is worth noting also that term premiums could, instead, stay low for longer than anticipated.	FS	FS
201504	1063	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Such an outcome would be a shock to investors who have positioned themselves for rising yields and could also lead to a further buildup of vulnerabilities if investors are driven to “reach for yield.”	FS	FS
201504	1064	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Other potential shocks of note that have been around for a while include a disorderly Greek exit from the euro zone, significant geopolitical disruptions, or distress at a large global financial firm brought about by, say, legal penalties.	FS	FS
201504	1065	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	I will conclude my prepared remarks by noting a few policy initiatives that the staff are pursuing related to specific financial vulnerabilities, which appear at the top of the final exhibit.	FS	FS
201504	1066	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	With regard to interest rate risk, the staff are independently measuring the risks at banks and working with those banks to manage their exposures.	FS	FS
201504	1067	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	On market liquidity, the staff are undertaking a variety of projects to better understand changes in the structure of bond markets, including increased electronification, and are working with other agencies to prepare a public report on the Treasury market.	FS	FS
201504	1068	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Regarding asset managers, the staff have begun evaluating the potential for the growth of managers’ activities, perhaps through the use of leverage and liquidity transformation, to contribute meaningfully to systemic risk and whether reforms are needed.	FS	FS
201504	1069	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Finally, on leveraged loans, supervisors continue their monitoring efforts and will begin a more comprehensive Shared National Credit review in May.	FS	FS
201504	1070	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	Thanks.	FS	FS
201504	1071	2015-04-29	meeting	GALLIN	That concludes my remarks.	FS	FS
201504	1072	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thanks.	FS	FS

201504	1132	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	That’s largely because of the energy price run-up in the mid-2000s.	12	1
201504	1133	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	I think we didn’t project that, and I think that’s why the solid line, the median, is above the data there.	12	1
201504	1134	2015-04-29	meeting	MESTER	But even the distribution looks like—	12	1
201504	1135	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Yes.	12	1
201504	1136	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	Again, I think that’s because of the energy price shock.	12	1
201504	1137	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	This is a relatively short sample with which we calculate standard errors around for PCE inflation, for two reasons.	12	1
201504	1138	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	One is, we don’t have data going back a long way, and two is, we think that this is a period over which inflation had different properties—it was more stable recently than in previous periods.	12	1
201504	1139	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	So, because of that, I think the influence of energy prices is more prominent here than it might be in the longer run.	12	1
201504	1140	2015-04-29	meeting	ENGEN	If I could add just one thing that amplifies that point, if you look in the middle right at core PCE, the median and the projected paths are virtually on top of each other, which is another way of showing that the total is being influenced by the run-up in energy prices and how it feeds into total inflation.	12	1

201504	1146	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If the FOMC were to introduce a new inflation target that was higher, would that have a higher gravitational pull in the staff’s model that we’d be pulled back to that higher target?	12	1
201504	1147	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	In terms of modeling and the way we do it in the FRB/US model, I think the answer is “yes,” because we do have a small term that reflects the FOMC’s stated target relative to current underlying inflation.	12	1
201504	1148	2015-04-29	meeting	WASCHER	I think it would be gradual, but I think in the FRB/US model, it would be a stronger attractor than a 2 percent target.	12	1

201504	1158	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren, do you want to start us off?	FS2	
201504	1159	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	FS2	
201504	1160	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	When I talk to asset managers in Boston, the biggest concern raised is the problem of liquidity in the secondary market for corporate bonds.	FS2	
201504	1161	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	They worry that when we begin to raise rates, a rush to sell positions in corporate bonds will occur, and a crowded exit with few buyers could lead to a rapid increase in the yield on corporate bonds.	FS2	
201504	1162	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	At least some elements of this concern probably deserve greater attention.	FS2	
201504	1163	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, the average size of trades in corporate bonds has fallen significantly relative to the average size of trades prior to the financial crisis.	FS2	
201504	1164	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This may reflect an actual or perceived difficulty in transacting large trades due to weakened liquidity in the market.	FS2	
201504	1165	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This raises the concern that if a significant portfolio rebalancing were to occur, it may be difficult to sell large positions in a timely manner.	FS2	
201504	1166	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, there has been a significant decline in the corporate bond holdings of broker- dealers.	FS2	
201504	1167	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	According to the SEC’s FOCUS reports, while J.P.	FS2	
201504	1168	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Morgan held $29.5 billion in corporate securities in 2007, those holdings had plummeted to only $11.3 billion by the end of 2014.	FS2	
201504	1169	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, Credit Suisse held $30 billion in corporate securities in 2007, and their holdings collapsed to only $4.4 billion by the end of 2014.	FS2	
201504	1170	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Such sizable declines in corporate securities holdings among these key liquidity providers lends some credence to the concern about potential liquidity problems in this market.	FS2	
201504	1171	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Third, bond mutual funds—which were shown in the earlier charts on financial stability—and bond exchange-traded funds have grown significantly since the financial crisis.	FS2	
201504	1172	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The exchange-traded funds pose a particular problem if investors view them as highly liquid.	FS2	
201504	1173	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	At the end of 2008, assets under management at exchange-traded bond funds totaled $57 billion.	FS2	
201504	1174	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	By the end of February this year, assets under management at exchange-traded bond funds had soared to $320 billion.	FS2	
201504	1175	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If investors assume that the corporate bond market is liquid and, more specifically, that their exchange-traded fund shares will always be liquid, and if they choose to sell as we tighten, they may be surprised at the price at which they transact.	FS2	
201504	1176	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In summary, the concerns with corporate bond market liquidity as we approach liftoff bear watching.	FS2	
201504	1177	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The degree of movement out of bonds is likely to be highly sensitive to the projected pace of tightening as well as to the timing of tightening.	FS2	
201504	1178	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	An oversized reaction in this market could result in a bumpy exit from the zero lower bound.	FS2	
201504	1179	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	FS2	
201504	1180	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	FS2	
201504	1181	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	May I ask Eric a question?	FS2	
201504	1182	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Yes, sure.	FS2	
201504	1183	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Eric, can you take it a step further and say what the implications of your concerns are for policy?	FS2	
201504	1184	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Is it for monetary policy?	FS2	
201504	1185	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Are you advocating a relaxation of capital requirements?	FS2	
201504	1186	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	No, I am not advocating a relaxation of capital requirements.	FS2	
201504	1187	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	I didn’t think so.	FS2	
201504	1188	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I think it highlights that how we communicate around the time of liftoff actually is critically important for whether people decide that this is something they need to do—to rebalance their portfolios quite quickly.	FS2	
201504	1189	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I think the way that financial stability interacts with monetary policy is, it highlights that the communication issues become pretty important.	FS2	
201504	1190	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	That’s helpful.	FS2	
201504	1191	2015-04-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thanks.	FS2

201504	1193	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	All right.	FS2	
201504	1194	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	FS2	
201504	1195	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	FS2	
201504	1196	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I want to thank the staff for the excellent assessment of financial stability.	FS2	
201504	1197	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s my reading that the assessment again indicates that current policy has not produced any material signs of financial instability.	FS2	
201504	1198	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Indeed, it appears that the main financial-instability consideration for monetary policy at the moment is that a near- term increase in the target range for the federal funds rate could lead to financial instability.	FS2	
201504	1199	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As the report says, “Term premiums in benchmark US and other advanced economy bond yields are again near historical lows reached before the taper tantrum, raising the risk of similarly outsized market reactions at liftoff.”	FS2	
201504	1200	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The staff also identified a vulnerability that could propagate this shock from the increase in rates.	FS2	
201504	1201	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Specifically, page 4 of the assessment notes that changes in the structure of the Treasury market could amplify the effects of an initial rate move and lead to sudden swings in prices and liquidity.	FS2	
201504	1202	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, how can we best mitigate this risk?	FS2	
201504	1203	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	President Rosengren, I think, highlighted one way to think about this, which is through communication, but I have a slightly different perspective on the answer to this question.	FS2	
201504	1204	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To answer this question, I think we have to understand why long-term rates might rise dramatically in response to a small increase in short- term rates.	FS2	
201504	1205	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And here I believe that a key consideration is the policy signal associated with such a move in the near term.	FS2	
201504	1206	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Raising the federal funds rate in the near term would mean they’re initiating liftoff when inflation is far below target and the growth outlook has been weakening.	FS2	
201504	1207	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Liftoff in such an environment would indicate that the FOMC is considerably less willing to provide accommodation to respond to adverse shocks than financial market participants currently anticipate.	FS2	
201504	1208	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As a result, they would expect less accommodation in general but especially so in bad times, and this expectation of higher interest rates and lower bond prices in bad times translates directly into higher term premiums.	FS2	
201504	1209	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, it’s tempting to conclude that we can somehow mitigate this potential financial instability only through reassuring verbal communication at the time of liftoff, but I think it’s difficult for words to trump the communication content of our actions.	FS2	
201504	1210	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So, in my view, we can best mitigate this financial stability risk by ensuring that our actions are always clearly connected to our pursued, declared objectives.	FS2	
201504	1211	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the current context, that would mean deferring liftoff until the economic data clearly indicate that raising interest rates is necessary for the FOMC to achieve its declared objectives of 2 percent inflation and maximum employment over the medium term.	FS2	
201504	1212	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll say more about what this conclusion means for our policy deliberations tomorrow.	FS2	
201504	1213	2015-04-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	FS2

201504	1285	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201504	1286	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Recent economic data have had a distinctly weaker tone since our previous meeting.	13	1
201504	1287	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The March employment report indicated little overall improvement in labor markets, the unemployment rate was unchanged, and payroll employment growth was surprisingly weak.	13	1
201504	1288	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, wage and price data have yet to show a clear trend toward our 2 percent inflation goal.	13	1
201504	1289	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While some of the weakness can be attributed to the severe weather in some parts of the country, many of the higher-frequency data before and after the harsh winter weather have also been on the soft side.	13	1
201504	1290	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a result, in my view, neither of the conditions for liftoff articulated in the March FOMC statement has been sufficiently met at this time.	13	1
201504	1291	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The March Summary of Economic Projections reflected some significant changes in longer-run variables.	13	1
201504	1292	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The central tendency of the longer-run unemployment rate has slipped from a range of 5.2 to 6 percent in June 2012 down to 5 to 5.2 percent in March.	13	1
201504	1293	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, participant estimates of the long-run equilibrium federal funds rate have declined.	13	1
201504	1294	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The central tendency in June 2012 ranged from 4 to 4½ percent, but now it is down to only 3½ to 3¾ percent.	13	1
201504	1295	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our assessment of these key variables has changed significantly, which, in retrospect, is not surprising, considering changes in demographics and productivity since the financial crisis.	13	1
201504	1296	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I and many other participants have lowered our estimates of one of our dual mandate goals—the natural rate of unemployment—we have not engaged in any comprehensive discussion of our other goal, the inflation target.	13	1
201504	1297	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	That target has remained unchanged at 2 percent since it was adopted in 2012.	13	1
201504	1298	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	We have learned a great deal about conducting monetary policy in a low-inflation environment since 2012.	13	1
201504	1299	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am fully aware that we should have a high threshold for changing our inflation target, as frequent changes would undermine its usefulness.	13	1
201504	1300	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But the accumulated weight of economic experience suggests, in my view, that a reexamination of our inflation target is warranted for several reasons.	13	1
201504	1301	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, the choice of an inflation target was largely based on research both here and abroad, indicating that the likelihood of reaching the zero lower bound and the cost of being at the zero lower bound was small.	13	1
201504	1302	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This research suggested a relatively low probability of reaching the zero lower bound, typically below 5 percent, and relatively brief spells at the lower bound once reached, usually a couple of quarters.	13	1
201504	1303	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In part, this optimistic read could have been based on faith in the efficiency of alternative monetary policy tools.	13	1
201504	1304	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, the experience of the past decade has been less favorable.	13	1
201504	1305	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Today most major developed countries are at the zero lower bound, and, despite employing alternative policy tools, none has yet exited, even though we are now more than six years past the financial crisis.	13	1
201504	1306	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In short, the research on the expected cost of hitting the zero lower bound has not been consistent with the economic outcomes we have observed.	13	1
201504	1307	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Second, we have revised our assessment of variables that should affect the probability of hitting the zero lower bound.	13	1
201504	1308	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The most obvious example is the lowering of the equilibrium federal funds rate.	13	1
201504	1309	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	With the same inflation target, a decline in the equilibrium federal funds rate should increase the probability of hitting the zero lower bound.	13	1
201504	1310	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The most recent SEP submissions, for example, report a decline in the equilibrium real rate of more than 50 basis points, and this assessment is echoed among private forecasters and market participants.	13	1
201504	1311	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If one of the rationales for setting a positive inflation target is to reduce the frequency of hitting the zero lower bound, a lower equilibrium real rate implies the need for a higher inflation target to reduce this probability.	13	1
201504	1312	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	On a practical note, the fact that Japan, the United Kingdom, Europe, and the United States have each hit the zero lower bound and have remained there for a very long time should make us wonder whether the global convergence to a value of 2 percent for the inflation target was misguided.	13	1
201504	1313	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Third, we have learned more about the cost of being at the zero lower bound.	13	1
201504	1314	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	After more than six years, we have still not returned to the 5 to 5.2 percent unemployment rate range that the SEP central tendency currently indicates is consistent with longer-run unemployment rates.	13	1
201504	1315	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While the new tools of quantitative easing—purchasing mortgage-backed securities and lengthening the maturity of our holdings—have resulted in growth faster than we otherwise would have experienced, we have missed both elements of our mandate for more than six years now.	13	1
201504	1316	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This is not an acceptable outcome.	13	1
201504	1317	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The consequences of not being able to exit the zero lower bound more quickly have been a long period of underutilized resources and below-target inflation that risks eroding the credibility of the central bank.	13	1
201504	1318	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	A higher inflation target would surely have given us more room to lower real interest rates using our conventional policy tools, likely saving hundreds of thousands of jobs.	13	1
201504	1319	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Despite our willingness to alter other variables, we have not recently had a comprehensive review of our choice for the inflation target.	13	1
201504	1320	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In light of the accumulating evidence that inflation targets globally may have been set too low, this choice may have resulted in a great cost to the global economy in terms of lost economic output and employment.	13	1
201504	1321	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thus, we should have a fuller discussion of our choice for the inflation target before we set our longer- run strategies at the beginning of next year.	13	1
201504	1322	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In addition to the longer-run implications of the inflation goal for monetary policy, a higher inflation goal would have more immediate policy implications.	13	1
201504	1323	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Entertaining a higher inflation target would imply an even larger inflation shortfall, compelling us to wait even longer before lifting off.	13	1
201504	1324	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	A weaker version of this proposition suggests both that we should delay liftoff until we see clear evidence that inflation is increasing, and that we should be willing to entertain an inflation rate that exceeds our current target.	13	1
201504	1325	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This strategy would, of course, be akin to price- level targeting, a notion that President Evans and others have previously discussed.	13	1
201504	1326	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In summary, we should recognize that the economy’s performance over the previous six years has a bearing not only on our estimates of full employment and the equilibrium federal funds rate, which many of us have adjusted in the SEP, but also on the inflation target.	13	1
201504	1327	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I understand the concern with shifting an inflation target that we set after years of deliberation and following years of success in bringing inflation down.	13	1
201504	1328	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But our failure to hit either of our mandated goals for six years and running demonstrates the potential cost of an inflation target that is too low.	13	1
201504	1329	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Recognizing the many complications that a change in the target would entail, I believe we should have a more fulsome discussion about what the previous decade of economic history has taught us about the optimal inflation rate.	13	1
201504	1330	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Should we be willing to entertain an increase in the inflation goal, this would, of course, have implications for the timing of liftoff, which we will be discussing tomorrow.	13	1
201504	1331	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201504	1332	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	13	1
201504	1333	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I would like to ask President Rosengren a question.	13	1
201504	1334	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You are implying that the only margin for adjustment is on the inflation target rate.	13	1
201504	1335	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Presumably there is another margin for adjustment, taking a lot of steps to make a future financial crisis of the type that we experienced in 2007, 2008, and 2009 less likely, right?	13	1
201504	1336	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Because you could argue that one reason why we are in this position is because we had a really, really bad financial crisis.	13	1
201504	1337	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So, in principle, one could take steps to make the probability of a financial crisis lower, and that would presumably lessen the need to change the inflation target.	13	1
201504	1338	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	How do you think about that?	13	1
201504	1339	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	If you think you can significantly change the probability or amplitude of those shocks, then you are right.	13	1
201504	1340	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But the equilibrium federal funds rate has come down quite a bit.	13	1
201504	1341	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Our own internal estimates of what that implies for how frequently we will hit the zero lower bound are that it is substantially higher given that most of the time the equilibrium federal funds rate that many of those models were estimated on was 4½ percent.	13	1
201504	1342	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	We are now at 3½ percent—I actually think you could make an argument that it is lower than 3½ percent.	13	1
201504	1343	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	So if you have an equilibrium federal funds rate that is lower, the implication is that you hit the zero lower bound more frequently unless you think you can dramatically alter either the frequency or severity of having the kind of shocks that we experienced.	13	1
201504	1344	2015-04-29	meeting	YELLEN	Isn’t it the case that some of the steps we would take to reduce the odds of a financial crisis—strengthening capital and liquidity—may actually, by raising the cost of intermediation, lower the equilibrium real rate?	13	1
201504	1345	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Yes, I think that’s right.	13	1
201504	1346	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But my point is just that the room you need depends on the size of the shocks that you are dealing with.	13	1
201504	1347	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And if you do other things and reduce the size of shocks, that also should be a factor.	13	1
201504	1348	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t really disagree with a lot of the points that you made, but it seems to me that that’s not the only potential margin—	13	1
201504	1349	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Yes.	13	1
201504	1350	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I’d just raise one other countervailing argument that, certainly, the experience around October 15 of the very sharp movement in financial markets at a time when no real economic news was occurring makes me wonder—I am not convinced yet that all of the actions we have taken have necessarily, dramatically changed the probability or likely severity of shocks in the future from what we experienced before.	13	1
201504	1351	2015-04-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In that shock, though, implications for the real economy were trivial.	13	1
201504	1352	2015-04-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In that case.	13	1

201504	1367	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Moving right along.	13	1
201504	1368	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201504	1369	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Over the intermeeting cycle, my staff conducted 56 interviews separate from our board meetings.	13	1
201504	1370	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We focused the interviews on any indications in their businesses that would confirm the weakness indicated by first-quarter data and, more to the point, suggest that first-quarter weakness might persist.	13	1
201504	1371	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We found that overall business sentiment remains quite positive, somewhat at odds with our reading of the incoming data.	13	1
201504	1372	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	On balance, our contacts and directors portrayed demand as continuing to improve at a steady pace.	13	1
201504	1373	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We noted, however, that compared with the previous cycle, their optimism is accompanied by a hint of caution.	13	1
201504	1374	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We heard more reports of negative effects of the dollar.	13	1
201504	1375	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Exporters, port operators, and firms with significant foreign operations all noted market or other challenges that they attributed to the dollar.	13	1
201504	1376	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	As expected, we heard reports of investment pullback and layoffs in oil and gas exploration and production firms as well as in oil services companies.	13	1
201504	1377	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	That drag is being partially offset by greater investment activity in business sectors benefiting from low energy prices.	13	1
201504	1378	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We also continued to hear reports that firms are trying to hold on to margin improvement coming from fuel and other commodity cost declines.	13	1
201504	1379	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Declines in gasoline prices have yet to translate into a meaningful boost in consumer spending.	13	1
201504	1380	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	A director with knowledge of consumer markets commented that product categories that historically have been leading indicators of stronger consumer activity—to wit, apparel, eating outside the home, and movies—have not yet signaled an upturn.	13	1
201504	1381	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We received positive reports on real estate investment activity, both commercial and residential.	13	1
201504	1382	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Architects and contractors indicated improved pipelines.	13	1
201504	1383	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Our banking contacts report that new mortgage and investment activity is strong.	13	1
201504	1384	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Regarding employment, we heard continued concern about turnover and retention.	13	1
201504	1385	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	At the same time, we detected little change in reports this round regarding wage inflation.	13	1
201504	1386	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	On that subject, although most data indicate that the trend in nominal wage growth remains flat, a measure constructed by my staff from the Current Population Survey does show an acceleration in year-over-year wage growth in the first quarter.	13	1
201504	1387	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Wage growth increased to a 3 percent pace in the first quarter, up from 2.8 percent in the fourth quarter and up from 2.4 percent a year earlier.	13	1
201504	1388	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Continuing on employment, I’ll mention something we heard for the first time from three large employers in quite different businesses.	13	1
201504	1389	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	All said they have begun shifting their work forces away from part time toward full time.	13	1
201504	1390	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	They all cited the high managerial and logistical cost and quality challenges of a large, part-time workforce.	13	1
201504	1391	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We’ve been struggling to reconcile these generally positive anecdotal reports with the hard data on the first quarter and early indications of second-quarter performance.	13	1
201504	1392	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Our tracking estimate of first-quarter GDP growth is just marginally above zero, at the low end of the spectrum presented in the Tealbook.	13	1
201504	1393	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Our tracking model is a straight statistical model with no judgmental overrides.	13	1
201504	1394	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We would not claim it’s the most accurate read of the first quarter, but it’s what the raw data are telling us, and we’ll have an official reading soon enough—tomorrow morning.	13	1
201504	1395	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	At this point, I’m holding to the view that weather and other factors played a significant role in first-quarter weakness, and that significant payback can be anticipated in the current quarter.	13	1
201504	1396	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We also observed—and this is nothing more than an observation—that weak first-quarter growth has been a pattern during the recovery, normally giving way to a stronger rest of the year.	13	1
201504	1397	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We’ve made a small adjustment to our full-year GDP growth forecast to reflect a weaker first quarter, but otherwise we have kept our forecast for growth and inflation unchanged from the March meeting.	13	1
201504	1398	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We made no material change to our outlook.	13	1
201504	1399	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We have growth resuming a run rate between 2½ and 3 percent, with second-quarter growth above 3 percent.	13	1
201504	1400	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	A strengthening of consumer activity from the first quarter is a key factor in our outlook.	13	1
201504	1401	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	We currently judge the risk to our growth and inflation outlooks as tilted to the downside.	13	1
201504	1402	2015-04-29	meeting	LOCKHART	With the greater uncertainty I perceive at this juncture, the Tealbook alternative scenario titled “Persistent Slowdown in Economic Activity” captures my concern that my outlook may be overly optimistic.	13	1
